O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, three sons, I have fulfilled this book that is beyond the science of medicine and has assembled its fulfillment in it, and has made the end through its exposings and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in vision that I have fulfilled this with this method, which is from the work of hands, and it is to know "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is troubled in our region and is all overturned, if it is perished by the science and craft, and there is nothing more to do than the small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And this is how the error and vanity have come about, and the intentions are closed and science is alienated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	I seem to think that I will revive this ordinance of this cauterization according to the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I will bring together the forms of the sharp-edged instruments of cauterization, and other tools of the work with the alignment of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is their craft.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled hands masters are found in our time, the art of medicine is elongated.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who enters this science to surpass in anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of the bones, and the forms and conjunctions and separations of the parts, and has knowledge of the bones, nerves, and tendons, and the number of joints, and the dementia and movable and resting bones, and the issue of their offspring.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason, Iocras says that the non and the evil are not together, and with the will is little; and at the same time in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	In the introduction of this book, we say that who does not know the things before said, if he is not careless in error and does not take the men; therefore I have often seen these who are involved in this science and if they abandon this science and sense experiment.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I see a madman who cuts off my aposteme from scrophules or the neck of a woman, and cuts the arteries of the neck; because so much blood issues out that the woman died in her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And see I another case where a wound of a man's ear was treated, and the wound was large; if it was removed with a piece of the bladder, and he died within three years.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	I have often been called to treat this wound, and I see the position of the patient and the size of the wound, and if it was not cut properly, he died.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see I another case where the king of our land, who had a broken leg, was treated with a fracture and plaster; and the patients were ignorantly constrained to keep the fracture in place as long as possible, and not leave any part of the leg exposed, and finally it was terminated; and he commanded that it should not be unwrapped; and later, when the leg was completely encased in plaster and the foot, it came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I am called to come to him, and I hurried to come remove the leg; and when I dislocated it if it was in pain and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all ways of the corruption were already confirmed or member, and could not be healed; and the corruption did not stop until the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see another wonder that collapses enchantment, and then ignites by the malice of his lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For chancre, when it is free of melancholic matter, only then can one touch it with iron if it is not part of the limb that can heal what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	1. And therefore, three-year-old girls, you should know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: it is skill, whether or not there is risk in other arrangements; and I will show each page of this book where there is fear and risk.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	1. And therefore, take care that you keep your hands clean, so that the folk may not speak ill of you. If you take up arms, use them lightly and firmly, and use the best way you can for the grace of God to help you come to salvation and be strong; and let the loathsome diseases of grief be cured; and keep your arms in order so that you may not be accused of coming from this world to another for glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen's advises in his warnings: "Do not take medicine from unqualified practitioners, lest you be deceived by fraudulent charlatans.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have found this treatise to consist of three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauterization and medicinal cauterization, and it is ordered from the head down to the feet; it covers the forms of strangulation, cauterization instruments, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and pricking, and ventouses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; it covers the forms of strangulation and all that is necessary in the work.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered by the main doctor's hands, and the forms of the surgeries.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	However, if we remember our work, it is necessary that I give the quality of the help and not harm to each complexity.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the help, and not harming, is the longest word and the most subtle science and the secret remedy; and for this they speak more of the wounds, and agree on this; and they are few in their words because I doubt the longevity.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization helps universally with all complexions or matters, but for the complexions: it is to know hot complexions with matter, and dry complexions with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions, all cauterization is useless and they say that cauterization is not helpful; the other says the opposite: that cauterization is only useful for diseases that come from chills and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used for hot diseases caused by chills or dryness; but those who say the opposite that cauterization helps great with hot diseases that come from the courage of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you perceive the heart of the patient and its moisture at the complexion of hot fire, you should quickly close the heart.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it at any time by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And all paths, no one intermeddles more than he who has experienced it, and knows by long use of the cauterizing chapter, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and their symptoms and the extent of tensions; for other complexions, we have no knowledge, even in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And they were found to fit and agree with the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Know, children, that cauterization is a secret of the healing arts, and more benefit than hot medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and only comes to harm when it reaches the member that is cooked, and does not harm any other part.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Hot medicines come from one part to another by aloofing, and bring diseases of grief to the healthy state; and by chance, if the fire has too much for its substance and its goodness, it does not harm at all, if it has no superfluity.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	1. And I found this in my research through experiment and the length of service and the study I have dedicated to the art, and it is true for things; and for this I apologize for the length of the language, as I only want to share with you the secret that is hidden or fire, and the quality of the work, as it treats the diseases of the body, just as the philosopher says in demonstrating; or receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	2. Know, son, that the cauteries should be made with the right tools and materials.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	3. I say that cauterization is useful in all cases, because the wounds are not well managed by the help of the cauterization; and moreover, if the cauterization is done for necessary pains and hastates that cannot wait for the time when the greatest malice does not come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	1. And never think, it is a foolish thing, if it follows the example of the fool; for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return; and he says thus, but it is not so if one takes care, because cauterization is only a medicine that dries the complexion, and drys the humors that cause pain, and is worthy of medicine for its haste in its work and its chivalry and its nobility.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	2. And it is possible that the disease returns never according to the complexion of the patient and the wound of the disease and its virtue; and they are assembled in him the superfluities by the acquisition of meat and similar things, if not cauterization is administered to him or he has little excess and moisture, like cauterization for pain, and the similar things, and part of the pain does not return often; but this is rare.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand that cauterization is a part of medicine, and this is seen; but they believe that cauterization is only after medicine, but we understand it is false, and cauterization is a part of medicine because when we know the ways of treating any disease and they are not effective, then we apply cauterization, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is well that cauterization is a part of medicine, but do not pay attention to the ignorant.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that gold-tipped cauteries were as harmful as iron ones, and they said this was due to the quality of the gold and its high substance. They said that gold-tipped cauteries do not cause poisoning, but it is true because I have experienced it and found that it is true in some people; and gold-tipped cauteries are as good as iron ones, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And when you hold the instrument of gold, you do not know if it is hot by the color of the gold, and it has cooled down; and if you heat it too much, it melts; then it becomes enough for prevention.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And that is why we use fire cauteries in our work, because we have not yet found a better way.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or if you have commanded this chapter of the lous head piercings, because it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	oil cauteries
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cauterization is used for moisture and cold on the lous head, and in it we do two things: by the cause of a disease called "soda", and by the cause of many humors that descend to the lous as ears, eyes, and for countless dreams and toothache and throat pain, and even for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, apoplexy, and coma, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cauterization is that if the physician purges it with solvent medicine altering the head III nuis or IIII, according to which virtues and ease and accustomed pain the patient can bear; then cut off the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then set the knife between your hands, and press it; afterward put the root of your palm tree between the root of his thumbs on his two fingers; and if you have two means, if you bleed, then squeeze the cauterization called "olivare," which is of this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. And place the knife at the joint, and make a descent and tension with your hand frequently; then gently hold your hand, and see if you can feel the bone slightly; if you cannot, continue the cauterization until you feel the bone as I have told you; afterwards take some tweezers, and put on a piece of soft cotton, and place it on the knife, and let it rest for three days; afterwards put on a moistened bandage; and leave it as long as the wound is healing; afterwards cure the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they said to the ancient one that as the wound becomes older, it purges itself; and therefore it helps.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these said that the fire cautery should be so tight that part of the bone is cut, and then remove what is cut from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say that the fire cautery should be so tight that it pushes the bone out, and if it is too large, as women do in their fuses because the humors come out outside; and it should be left for a long time overstretched; after that it should be treated and sutured.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	1. These two methods of cauteries do not seem less effective in general, despite any fear or doubt in anyone; and it seems to me that I should leave them; for the head of the shoulder is weakened by continuous natural solutions, as we have experienced in other parts of our body; and even when the patient's strength is weak by nature, the first appearance of cauterization appears more salving and less painful to me, and therefore I use it accordingly.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	2. of the ancient pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	3. When throughout the head there is chronic pain, and it lasts for a long time, if one must use pills and ointments called "cochies" and purges of the head and oils and plasters; and when the cauterization is done as we have said before, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	The head of the patient is of great nature, and it should not be too cold; therefore, we recommend using fire cautery on that part.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After treating each corne of the eye with fire cautery, as we have mentioned before, and then treat the area called "vascular" which is where the veins are located; and these are the ones that are put under pressure; and hold your hand so you can see the bone: the patient feels too much pain in this cautery than in others, and I will explain further; and it is necessary that the cautery points be more sensitive than those used for the cauterization of the chief, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	1. "For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	2. "For in one part of the fire cautery, there comes sudden pain, and it spreads to the entire body, and the head is purged with medicines, and other cures have been made as I have said in the division of diseases, and all of this does no good: therefore, I have done cauterizations in two ways, that is, with hot and dry medicine.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	3. "If you have a poultice of alum, and the wound oozes and becomes infected, and then you sew up the head where the pain is, and afterwards make the temple so that you can put the poultice of alum back on; and when it is put back on, if the patient holds the poultice well and leaves it for 12 hours, and then removes it and applies the ointment of cotton, leaving the wound for 2 to 3 days; then you cover the wound with a warm damp cloth until the swelling goes down.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of inflammation, when it is healed; and if you see that there are no curative drugs that I have written or treated other curative drugs.

Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then resume the fire cautery again and as many times as you can, and let it remain for three days; then put cotton wool on the dressing, and apply the drying ointment as soon as it is healthy, and after 40 days have passed, if it is still healthy, then apply an ague corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and follow according to what comes in your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterization of fistulas that no of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understands the fistula, and then in the furnace put the subtle cream of coi; after that forms the shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make it to the quantity of a .З. of plonc; and hold your hand or the cream firmly, and do not move the patient at all, that the ploncs melted do not go to their oil; and it is necessary to put the oil on the clean cotton wool in the eye-hole or in the ear: the plonc if it is hard in the fistula, and the health of the patient improves.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	If the fistula is healed by the cauterization we have mentioned, it's good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer tincture of mercury to the umbilicus, and bring the fistula back to its original position according to what is appropriate for the patient's own belly.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks in the lips are called "tears," and also in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks according to what we have mentioned in divisions, and the patient does not benefit, then use a small cauterization iron according to this form:

de l’aposteme de la goule	2. of the abscess of the gall
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	3. When the abscess of the gall comes in the root of the gall or in the ute, or in the teeth, or in the roots of the teeth, and it becomes inflamed and forms a fistule; and you cure it as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit: therefore, it is necessary that you have a fire cautery according to the size of the fistule; after the bote or peritonis of the fistule, and hold your hand until the gall comes out of the font of the leu, and if it does not come out, once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in the cures, as soon as it is healthy; and if it is cured once or twice, it is good; and if not, it is necessary to open the leu and extract the corrupt bone, according to what you will find in your chapter.
dou movement des dens	The first sentence to translate is "Ou cautere de
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicines and it does not help, then place the patient's gauze in your mouth; afterwards wash the cauterization that was made on you in this way, as if you were putting a collar around the tooth; and remove the teeth from the cauterization with force, and hold your hand tightly with the pain at the root of the tooth; afterwards gently release your hand and continue the cauterization according to your will; afterwards fill the mouth with salty water, and rinse for an hour and then spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in a similar manner, the teeth that were moving are confirmed, and the gum becomes soft and restrained, and the moisture is dried out.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When the pain of the teeth comes from cold, or if it is cold or visible, and the remedies of medicine are ineffective, then it has become necessary to have a cauterization done in two ways: either with a burning iron or with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with a hot iron if it is such that you can burn wool with it, and the end in a piece of iron or steel; then take cotton and wrap it around the point of a needle, and moisten it with brimstone, and put it on the painful tooth firmly and hold it until it cools down; and often I do this as long as the virtue of the root of the tooth lives, and if you see that the wool and cotton are burned in brimstone, and put it on the painful tooth, and put on the iron charred as much as the fire reaches to the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	1. When the fire cautery is applied, if it is as hot as a piece of iron or copper, and is large enough to reach the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, after which form it according to this, and place it on the tooth, and hold your hand until the cautery is cool; do this often, as the pain will be less for you or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	2. des scrophules	of scrophules
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrophules are wet and cold, and do not obey digestion with medicines, then clean the blade of the cautery after it comes out, and let the openings be for the smoke to escape from the other part; and place the blade on the abscess once, or as it is, until it comes out of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, then use the blade according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it for three days; and cover the wound with wet cloth as long as the wound ointments and poultices are needed.
Li forme de la cainne:	1. The form of the chain:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture is present in the urethra and at the same time when cold complexion comes, it is necessary that the patient be treated first with soluble medicines; after that, I perform a fire cauterization at the base of the throat, and you should not come too close to the throat, and do not burn more than a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez. de la toust	Of the entire body

de ydropisie	of dropsy.
