de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the ear infection
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that affects the ears is one of the four things: grains, fleas, mines or similar things like that; or seeds, like chickpeas, peas, and beans; or things that flow like sore throat, cough, and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it affects the ear with a hole or another way of thing that does not fit well in the ear, and does not grow in the ear, if you put the ear to the sun, it will dry and stop growing.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the piercing, if no drop of violet ointment or linseed oil is distilled, then the extraction is performed; I then apply pressure, and it stuns the nose when it is sneezing comes, and puts on the ear pieces of velvet or wool; and the ear is at ease.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	This treatment often comes out once; and if it does not come out, then the extraction is performed with fine tweezers, and this is its form:

de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the shaking of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien. Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes out of it, if one cannot see it, is a sign of the cure in many other situations, and in this case, it is necessary to put the ear that is sore with the salve; and look at: if you see the ointment apparent, then the olive has completely cured this swelling of the ear.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And so it is and cutting in front and behind all around, if it does not hurt the ear; if the exudate is of char or cors of the ear, if the hand as subtle pincers, and a light cape, as long as that char is entirely out.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the exudate is fully in the ear, then take a soft, light razor and gently scrape it, then put on a small amount of fire-scorched wax, then it is in the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the exudate that the patient feels is gritty in the ear, softly pierce, and be careful not to hurt the ear nerves; then put into the ear a tent according to the large opening of the ear, and the powder in the Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. de la gresle	Of the gallows
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times, things come in papers from the eyes that seem like gritty things in their form and hardness, and for this disease is called "granule," and it is an assembly of moisture large in the paper of these and soaked; the eyes are as follows: make sure if the granule moves on both sides, and it is a light thing to know; then make it wide, then scorch each part slightly, then take it with pincers, and the cape.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	1. Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	2. If the snow is descending towards the inner ear and covers the part below, if reversed, and the snow is grasped with tweezers, and presses from both sides; and if the paper is moved by incision, it does not hurt; and when the snow is removed, if the oily salt is leveled, and the skin of the patient is cared for as much as possible while the malaide is healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is obtained from the papers of the sheets, and this happens more as the children grow older, and it harms their hair, and they come to the candles in the mornings, and cannot see the light of the sun because the tears come to their hair; and for this they lie on their backs, and sleep, and are the sheets soaked with the exinach that the enflame and the appearance has covered with the exinach that is open in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you need to press the sheet against your two and feel the exinach inside of it.

des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai. It is necessary that you place the head of the patient's shoulder in your hand, then turn the paper of the oil to your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, then insert an awl into all the holes of the thread; and let the margin of the paper or the hair that comes from these hairs be on the left side of the paper, and turn the thread up; then cut off the part at the end of the paper, at the end of the hair, all around, from the largest to the smallest; then pull out the thread, and put a small piece of cotton and ribbon on the paper, then run your finger along the paper as if it were a needle, and if you see the figure is according to the quantity that you see rising the paper that is marked with a dot.

Then, begin with a small loop just next to the natural hair follicle as it grows in size, then pull out the root at one of the two angles, then scrape off the entire thing. puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then comes he who surpasses in equal measure according to the form that is here:

Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui. de la porriture de l’oil	Of the oil's fat
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, called "aleacrati" or oil comes in the form of grease, it can occur in two ways: naturally and unnaturally.

dou derrompement de toile uvee	Great shock of the eyelid
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When there is a shock in the eyelid, it opens wide and throws off small pieces of skin like resin; therefore, close your eyes and cut a thin thread at the root of the affected part, then cut another thread if there is a double thread in the part; and make sure, and leave the first thread according to its position, then cut the double thread and pull out a part of the eyeball, and hold it firmly, then remove the thread and put some ointment on the inside of the eyelid as much as the threads stick to the eye; and leave it until the threads are no longer stuck to the eyelid, and cure the ointment with comforting things as long as the wound is healing; and never again will the wound be restricted by any part of a circular piece of cloth as soon as it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hairs grow long and coarse, if they are pricked with a sharp needle that comes from the oil, and the moisture is driven out and the hairs fall out, and it heals; then they are plucked as soon as they are healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the oil's bow
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is only bowels assembled in the oil, resembling a sharp descent, but it is not sharp; and the manner of appearance of the disease if you make the patient sit at the side and right, then take the chief between your hands of II parts, and pull as much as you see the bowel coming to the desus of your hairs; then it is clean, and does not descend and is not combed out, and see the maladies things as if it was; and if it does not descend, say that it is sharp, and if the bowel descends is not assembled so as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you place the patient between your hands, then take the sharp spatula and make a small incision on the corneal surface, as far as the conjunctive continues with the cornea and the sclera, until the fluid comes out. And when it is done, if it distills in cold water mixed with honey, or hot ginger, then it should be treated with another remedy until it is cured.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil's waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the resemblance of the waters in the division, and when it is necessary to measure; if according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you hold the patient's hand tightly between your own, using the light of the sun, and feel the healthy and firm oil; then place the paper of the oil on your left hand so that the hairs are in order; or on your right hand so that the hairs are disordered; then take in your right hand, if the hairs are in order, the instrument called "almagda"; or in your left hand, if the hairs are disordered; then place the point of the instrument at the coronet through the largest part of the oil in the blenchor of the oil in the smallest part of the arm; then push the instrument called "almagda" firmly, and pull your hand as much as it penetrates the blenchor of the oil, and feel that almagda is working on the empty thing; and the measurement of the almagda hole should be at the end of the nose; and this is the coronet of the oil; if you see the bone in the paper for the clarity of the corner of the eyelid, and then place the instrument where it is needed, and press the oil firmly after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If it is now swollen, if he sees the surgeon before him and the instrument in his hand.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After the patient has rested for a short time, and if the swelling returns to the second duct, take the forceps with the instrument, and when they are firmly held and do not move, gently twist your hand a few times; then place a piece of cloth soaked in warm oil on the swollen part.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply warm oil to the soaked cloth or powdered ointment with enough urine and bind with the healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Yes, and those of us who are ours, we put on like poultry with much urine.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the maggot cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, because it lacks the necessary soft hairs, then you must use an instrument called "alberit" which has this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And by perforating only the conjunctive, and not too deeply, but making a small opening, then insert the maggot, as we have said; and at the end of the operation, the patient will feel some pain in the eye, and it will be dark in the socket; and you should make no movements, and feed light foods, and do not move the head to the left or right, and keep it according to its own disposition; then close the wound in this house of darkness, and examine your eyes, and show the patient any interesting things, and then replace the link as soon as possible after the ninth day; but it is necessary that you do this in the eye of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you remove it, because the swelling increases rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When the wound is stitched, you should gently apply oil to the stitch before the ninth day, and then cover it with a piece of cloth or linen to prevent any infection. Once it is healed, remove the stitch and cover it with a clean cloth or linen.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then, you should make a small incision in the house and convert it into its case; and advise that no disciples should undergo this procedure.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Then, some came from the region of Yrach who told us that in some places it was used as a remedy for the measles, but we have never seen any in our land, nor have we ever read about it in ancient books; and by chance, this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of amalgama, because those who do not know them properly; and they are truly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And be the heads of these same subtleties, and the tail in third angles ahead.
de la char sor le neis	of the sword and the knee.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No swords and knees are ever born or broken, and if there are any that seem like scorpions at the mouth of the foot; and if they are of such a kind or have a sword enchanced with flesh color, and if it is a sword of bone color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these swords which are not enchanted, and do not mie, it is necessary that you make the patient lie between your hands in the sun; and work on his nostrils, and cut the horn on those swords, and take them away; for that is what you can sustain in the subtle spatumile of one part, as long as you see that the sword is all steeled.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there is nothing else that can be done, and you examine all the wounds subtly and lightly, if it does not cause any harm; and if it does not cause any pain or swelling, and if it is not malignant, then cauterize as much as possible and burn until the wounds are charred and all the bones are burned, then gently touch it with wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If you can operate, and moisture comes to the palace, signifying that it is healthy; and if moisture does not penetrate as it should, signifying that it has charred in the bone of the wound, or that the wounds cannot be trimmed: therefore it is necessary to bind a piece of linen around the wound, using our hands, and it should be between every other nail or less; and put the surgeon's thread through the head of the nail as it grows, and tie it with odorant as it comes out of the mouth; and many times do this to the child in schools, and it is a light thing for him who sees it done; then hold the chief that comes through the nail with one hand, and the other chief that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and follow it after each other as we have seen.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	1. Until you know that the child has corrupted the char, then take the boy's penis, clean it, and make him urinate, and put the urine in an Egyptian poultice, and put it back in the urethra as before; do this 3 times or more, until the poultice corrodes all that is left of the char; then put a catheter made of cork for some days until it is healthy, and if he has knowledge of dried herbs, then use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the child's penis, or when it is distilled, the oils and medicines or urine.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	1. And let it be of silver or gold, resembling an overturned lamp, like a dog, and lead it thus; and if you see, if I make a dog close, and it has empty paws to expel the head, and have a handle for the head to hold when one heats the oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	2. of the char and the neck.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	3. Many times the head is affected with a disease called "telul", and grows and becomes large, until it is seen when looked at; and therefore it is necessary to cut at the beginning, and make the bone all raw, then put on the fire cautery or hot medicine; and if it is delayed as long as it is large, if it is hard, of a dark color, poor sense: if it is not touched by iron because it is enchanted, for when one touches it never comes any harm to the patient; and if the enchantment is of silver, not of iron, you will see that it can be covered, if the patient is cold and the cure is painful, and cure the patient of things drying and restricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated and reset
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	It is said that when solutions for continuation come from one of these cartilages, it does not last long and is not beneficial to any man.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary therefore to look at whether the wound is fresh at all its base; and then close the lips with a bandage, and treat it until it is healthy; and if the lips are already swollen on both sides, it is necessary that you scrape off all the parts of it as they become healthy, and then close the lips with a bandage, and extract, and powder with powder of dragon's blood, and burn incense; and put some pieces of a plaster of gold or other soothing plaster on the powder, and leave it until it sticks to it, and then treat the ointment as it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing if you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the belly stitching; or by thread, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	of the lips' abscesses
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	The lips' abscesses often cause pain, resembling grains of sand, and become larger or smaller; therefore, you should open the lips, and cut them asunder at each nose, and take out the pieces with tweezers and sew them in each part; then use the lee after the incision of vitriol, as long as it is not soaked; and then the lee of ointment, and cure the lip with dry things until it is sound.
de la char des gencives	Of the horse's knee
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times the knee cap has been injured in the horse's knee; what they call "albulus"; if you hold it with your fingers, and the root of the nail, and let go of the bone or sinew; then put on leather vitriol powder, or other restraining and desiccant powders; and if the knee cap returns after the incision, and many times it happens, if the cap is second time, and cauterized: if it does not return soon after the cautery; and these are the forms of strums in the horse's knee.
des sordens	of stones
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	1. No times are assembled at the head of the teeth, teeth between the cheeks, gums that are ugly and sharp; and no times is the black and yellow and crooked tooth, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and it becomes the yellow tooth; if you want to place the dentist between your hands, and its chips are in your holy, and open the teeth or gums as much as possible, until nothing more is done; and then I make black and green, and brown and other stains, as long as they are visible; and if this is in the first reason, it's good; but if not, if you repeat the second day and tooth, as long as you have everything back; and advise that the teeth have the ability to different forms of estructions to laugh, according to what the demonstration shows, because the raser that cleans the teeth has other shapes than those shown in the teeth; and these forms and others are with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	1. It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay and do not neglect it as much as possible, because it should not be made; for it is a substance of high juice therefore there is no excuse to delay.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	2. When the patient is forced to bear pain, it is necessary that you be certain of the tooth's will.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	3. Many times the patient's pain is endured, and it must be made sure that the tooth is in its place, and the tooth is burned; and it will not depart from the pain as long as the mouth is open, because we have already wanted to do this for these better ones; and when you are certain of the tooth's will, if you must scrape off all of the tooth, then use a spatula firmly to guard the gum of all parts; then the mouth has your needles at the first part and again, as they are well inserted, then they confirm the needles; and the head of the tooth is in your hand between your fingers, and it must be held so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the broken tooth, and if it does not break further, then take none of these strips and gently pull out from each side, and move it as you have done first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are felt and drawn out, then it is necessary to fill them with cloth, whether the holes are large or small; and if the extraction is done subtly with needles, which does not break the tooth; and it is wise to over the gum for removing the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be well prepared that you do not break the tooth, and there remains a part, and it goes to the patient through the malice of the root, more great pains of the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	1. And you should know that what they do is not like what ignorant healers do, who break the charm with their haste and their hardiness, and never cause any harm to anyone except what we have counted; but they cause it once by the agony of this great disease, either because of the roots they cut, or because of the charm they break, just as often as we want; and when the poison is in, if you wash the leeward with wine or alum and silk, and it comes out, it often comes out, if you use wine or vitriol; and if it does not come out, if it is cauterized.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tooth extractions, whether they are the first teeth or not, are long and wide at the tips and have large handles, so they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be of large size if they do not break when pulled, and they should be made of good iron, and they should have teeth to hold onto.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root of the tooth is broken during extraction, if it comes to pass that you put your finger into the hole with a soft cloth wet in warm water for a while.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the hole is smoothed, then pull out the points that are called "algefri", even if the head looks like a beak; and they should be made in the same way as a lime and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out through all these tines, then you must pull the root as far as possible, and then insert the instrument called "althali", which is a type of plow, with this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is very large and does not break the skin, and the root jumps over this, it is good; but if not, then you can use all the force you have, with these forms following:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you can use this instrument with two razors, then the form is:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other forceps that are in front of the teeth, and this instrument which seems like large pins, with this form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And so it is that the bone does not break, and the tools are sharp; and also other bones, which are not as strong; and the masters make the joints true by themselves with their own instruments, according to what their work and the disease demonstrate, for they have some diseases or the ancients did not teach any instrument for the diversity of bones or they break not at the right place or other bones, or they porridge, if he seeks the bones that he needs, and helps with gestures, as follows is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-holding to hold the bone, so it does not slip, but can hold and grasp; and then restore the part of medicines corresponding to this, and if there is in the bone porridge, and it is small, if all this instrument is:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears to not fit naturally in the gum, and it is misshapen, and even more so in women with multiple teeth, it comes to pass that you must cut away the tooth after the gum, and it is not rightly placed, and it cannot be sewn or merged: therefore, the gum; and if it is close with the tooth, then use this instrument whose form is like the small beak, and it should be of hard steel made sharp:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cut is quickly and quickly with your hands due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be merged, then you can merge it with a piece of gum like this:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is like the making of the eyes, and in the bone there is little and little by hands lightly, so that it does not move at all when it chicles; then the plain at the end has no rasor, and the teeth are too sharp and they bite the tongue, if it is made as even as possible, so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth are loose by pressure or by chewing, and the patient cannot press on it because it pains, and you treat them with restraining medicines, and it does not work; if it is restrained by a golden thread, for the silver wire becomes green and rots, but the gold does not hurt; and the thread should not be too thick or too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth, take the thread and the string double between the healthy teeth, then put the strings between the bad teeth, as long as you see improvement in the healthy tooth; then resume the covering on the part where you began, and gently and wisely move your hand, so that it does not move at all; and if your thumb is on the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	1. Then, the head of the nail is held by some needles, and they are assembled, and placed between the healthy tooth, and it is inserted as not to damage the tongue; and then it is left as narrow as it can be, and if it does not move, or the filaments come out, if the forceps are pulled by another thread; if it stays and serves for all its strength, and this is the shape of the teeth and the figure of the incisors of the second healthy teeth and the second molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	2. And when the tooth is set, if it is moved in its place, slightly, as we have said; and it does not become loose, nor is it painful, and never takes on the shape of a bone of a mare's hoof, and it is placed in the socket where it was, and if it fails, and is tightened as we have said, and it lasts and serves for all its strength:
de coper lou liien de la lengue	From the copper wire of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No time is lost that comes from the tongue or nature; or by accident of wounding; and the ovary is such that it opens the mouth of the midwife, and has its head in her mouth, and loosens the tongue; then cope the wire nervous large, as long as the tongue is loose from its hold, and if it bites or nout, and that is due to pain, if it bites the uncinate and cope large the other side; and keep that the fanger does not become too much too soon, for the artery that is out of place; and when you have done, if the leu is red and inflamed, or cold, then put the lingue between two linen tents; and the midwife will touch the patient's tongue every night, that the patient may be soothed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the dislocation occurs, if the patient is in pain, and if the cauterization is done slowly at the fire cautery, which is suitable for this, then the treatment of another treatment as soon as it is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that it is reddish or black and the patient does not feel pain, if it is not touched, because it is gangrene; and if it is declining into a blenchor, and it has moisture, if it oozes pus, and it forms a subtle spumous substance, and it delivers from one part and another; and if the patient does not feel pain in your care, if you apply vitreol broth as much as it is inflamed, then return to your care as soon as you treat all parts; then raise the leg with ailis and seal, and the treatment of other treatments as soon as it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat's abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never comes a gangrene of the throat's abscesses called "godath", and they are properly known as the "hammands". When you treat them, as we have said in the division, if they are not healthy, then keep them: they are hard, small in size, and pus-colored, if they do not touch iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, if it does not touch iron, then for the evacuation of blood; but let it remain until it is dead, and then you will take it out; and if it is of a bluish color and the root is fine, if you have prepared the instrument to cover it, but first look to see whether the abscess has closed and is quiet.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then fasten the patient in front of the sun, and let their head be in your hand, and make them open their mouth and press their tongue between their fingers, and press the lower lip evenly all around the instrument, regardless of whether it is made of silver or gold:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue evenly all around the instrument, and see if the incision is deep, then take the canine and the thumb in your mouth, and pull it towards the nail, and keep pulling until it comes out more than you put it in; and do not take anything from the tail with you, then place the instrument in the forceps, and regardless of whether it is made of silver or gold, it seems to have strengths; and all the teeth are sharp, and one part is against another, and they are very jagged, and it is made of iron or bronze:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if you have needles, then the form is as follows:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	Then, make a cut on one side and label the other end; when you have cut one of the hairs, cut the other in the same manner, and after making the incision, heat the blade with hot water, and wipe it dry, and if the hair comes out, if the hair is cooked, or if it is a piece of pomegranate rind that is cooked, or if it is a piece of mirtle, and similar things, until the blade is not stained; then cure it as soon as it is healthy; and never have any other abscesses born in the mouth than the two hairs, if you cut them like the two hairs.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	I am treating a woman with a wound that was causing her to choke on her food, which is called anaphylaxis; I had closed almost the entire throat, so she could not breathe through the tube that was blocked by saliva, and could not drink or eat, and she died if she stayed in this state for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	The wound was very severe, and I had to remove it with two incisions.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then removed the tooth and took out a large portion of the jawbone; I then removed another piece from the other socket, and closed the mouth and pressed on the tongue; after removing the tooth in these wounds, and taking out a small part, and only a little blood came out of the woman's throat, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop trimming the wound with long cuts; the wound gradually closed and filled the socket that I had made, so that it did not leak much; therefore I closed and cauterized the gum: after that, she recovered; I left these parts, and only God could do more for her.
de l’uve	From the urethra
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it comes out of the urethra, and it is long and thin, it is called 'perpendicular'; and if it is very large and curved, it is called 'the urethra'.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the incision does not benefit, and you see that the cauterant is soothing and subtle, and it is suitable to copulate; and that which is curved and not long is assembled and not far; and it is bloodshot or of a red or black color, and you should discard the incision of the wound.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, as I have said, to consider the patient's gut and length, that you place the patient in front of the sun, and press the tongue on the instrument we made note of before; then the forceps in the eye, and pull it out, and cut at the two points I mentioned in the incision of the two amandines.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you not cut more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more, you will hurt your voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we said in the incision of the two amandines, and cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of pain, then you must use an engine for the burning of the painful part.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of burning is sharp and quick.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place his head on your hand, and then press his tongue onto the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and confess with a sharp, living force; if it is not too thick or too clear, then use the edge of this instrument, and its form is:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has a lock of hair or a piece of medicine, as the teeth of a comb, and place the instrument in all the medicine on the eyeball; and the patient should be anxious about his chest, if the saliva and the mucus flow from his mouth with the medicine, if it does not reach the chin and neck, then keep your hand on all the medicine and press on the eyeball, as much of the half of an hour as you see the pain and the medicine's sting is eased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wet the cotton with the medicine, and push the instrument through the cotton in the tail of the catheter, as much as the cotton dries on the eyeball; and do this often, as long as the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and after four or five hours or six, if you have skill to renew the medicine cauterization, if it restarts, and after the cauterization of the medicine, wrap the pus around the eyeball with cotton, and clean what is around the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and use gargles as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, only cauterization; if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take calamus and sassafras and origin and chamomile and avon and similar herbs, and all or none of them in one pot, and mix, and make boil; and it can be well glued with hard earth, and the pot should have the instrument made according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it can be of silver or gold, and one of the heads is inserted into the mouth of the patient as much as the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, as long as the eye is anesthetized; after that, it often resumes, as long as the eye dries, and keep that you do not make this at the beginning of the onset of abscess gangrene, because many things come; and do not make this but at the decline of abscess gangrene.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	If this instrument is not present, then take a needle and sew the head of the shoulder with a thread of yarn, if the mouth of the patient has too much saliva; for the thread of yarn does not wet the tongue, and it is a good cure together with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened to the throat, either with a bone or a fish spine, or nothing at all; therefore, if you must see what is there, and press the tongue against the instrument as far as possible, so that you can see the thing; and if you do not open the mouth, it is necessary to make the patient vomit until the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance, if the thing is cleared through vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a morsel of dry bread; and then wrap it around the sponge, and then glutinate it; and when it reaches the mouth, if it opens, and then draw it out; and if it does not open from what we have said, then take the instrument of plucking according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	1. And let the forceps be placed at the root if possible, so that it may more lightly enter the mouth; keep the head upright; and avoid touching the epigastrium, as all will vomit; and make sure that the instrument does not pierce the bone; and if it does, either draw it back or pull it further along the instrument evenly, until it is fully inserted.
de la sansue de la gorge	2. of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	3. No time is lost in medicine when the throat is unobstructed, as I have said in the division, by the use of medicines; and when this does not help, look at the mouth of the patient in the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I have given you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	If you see the joint, if it has all its small bones, or if it has thin nails that are worth this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it is not worth it, if you take a hair of the dog, and pull on the mouth of the patient, then pull or cut the hair and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And the patient's face is covered with sweat all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full advantage of seeing cold sweat, and open the mouth, and the throat feels it is being swallowed, and move it often; and if the joint soon feels the heat, then do.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	If she does not understand as we have said, if the patient smokes tobacco, with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, as it will give relief.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	If the manner of the fumigation is that you prefer to use or if there are charcoals visible, and it is placed inside a covering of a cloth in the environment, and in that place is the head of the instrument; then perform your fumigation, and the patient places the end of the cainne in his mouth, closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not enter, but comes out the nose; and the nose will now be cleared, and if it does not clear, repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and drink salty and bitter things, and do not drink water; and then perform the task that you performed with this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument used to treat the gouge, if it is, when one can see, resembles tacks corbets to enter the mouth; and it resembles the beak of a surgeon, and has sharpness like lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot let go; and then the form is:
li chapistres des apostemes	The cauteries of the abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The appearances of the abscesses are, according to what is remembered in this book, and they are different in perforation and size; and there are two ways, one of which is its own appearance, and for that it is moist.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method if by the legs or if they are in the course.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the head of the chief is different from that of the foundation, and the head of the lower limb is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if in the judgment of the head there is no perception, as long as the bow is dead according to its accomplishment; and if for such things it is necessary to perceive when they are thought to be, and do not die according to their accomplishment, as much as those that are joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when the head comes from joints, and it is left as it is until it is completely erect, by chance if the ligament and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, because this is due to contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	1. If the wound is deep into the member, and you delay the piercing as long as possible, it will harm the primary member; or if it is the foundation, and the hole is not made until it is dead, then it is the foundation that cannot be made, and it may cause a fistula to open and become long-term; and it cannot heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	2. It is necessary that you clean the wound of the piercing of the cautery that is dead according to the completion, and when the pain is calmed, when the fever subsides, when the pain and bruising are eased, and there is a lot of sweating and restlessness, and the agitation of the head of the cautery, and other signs; and it is necessary that you sew the piercing or more dependent on the cautery, and where it was opened; and it should be a long wound, and if the cautery is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all of them equally or not, without clotting.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those places where they prick, according to the member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the flesh, if it is painful, then let the puncture remain until it is confirmed in digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you prick it beforehand, and the gall comes out of it, and it is painful to touch; and by chance they harden the lips and become more ugly from it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is no abscess that is pricked according to the size of the gall, according to what the member can bear.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you prick small abscesses, small pustules; and in large abscesses, large pustules, and many fangs according to the appearance of the abscess; and if in such abscesses or they are hard to touch, and close; when they become as hard as I am, and are dried out, then it is necessary to do so as with bubbles: and if in such cases that are cut at three angles, and if in such that are cut like the thorn of the marten, as with abscesses of the gall; and if in such that are made a small cut, and others of different sizes and appearances.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	1. Those who have no head, if it is only a superficial wound, it is necessary that you cut it gently; and when the wound is large and has a great hole, and it has pierced through the entire hole, but not all of it, then stop the wound in that hour, but in another part; then the wound stops at the other end, then no further damage is done; this is done many times with great care, as long as the hole is completely filled; at the same time, if the patient is weak in virtue, or a woman carries, or small children, or elderly people who are decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the expectations have never occurred once with the end of the bowel, that by chance the patient died, and you do not blame yourself.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you notice your abscess, if the wound is large, look at the size of the abscess; and if it is small, use a linen or cotton gauze; and if it is large abscesses and there is fever, then tie each one with a piece of cloth so that one covers the other; and if you have scratched a part of leather with the abscess, and it has grown, then cover it with fine silk or rags of linen, and the edge, and the care of the ointment as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	When the patient's temperature rises due to the fire cautery, if it becomes too cold and wet, and the skin is sore, and he should cover the affected area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient's temperature rises due to the fire cautery, and it becomes too cold and wet, and the skin is sore, and he should cover the affected area with many layers of clothing. If the patient's tongue is dry, and the eyes are nervous, then you should put on warm vinegar and oil-soaked bandages; if this is the case, and the lesion is charred, then you should put on wet vinegar and oil-soaked bandages, or wet wine and oil-soaked bandages, as we have said before; then remove the aposteme and the pus, and the cure, as it is necessary, until the patient is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	This comes when you have to know the overall treatment of abscesses: or you have said how one must come before the treatment of abscesses, and now this chapter.
des soros	of sore
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When sore wounds come and are like the bite of a grape vine, and are similar in appearance to this one.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	If it is fat and of such that it has moisture, or like the grape vine; and if it is such that it is hard and rough in the cutting, and it does not have doubt, then it will not be opposite.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the measurements of the size if it is that you stretch to all the instruments that are called "intermuscular," of which the form comes after, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they are made longer by suspension.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.
