And when the moisture is seen, it should not be shorn if it has any hair containing that moisture, because it will return again as soon as it is left alone; then dip the cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; otherwise, use warm and cold water, and apply the wound, and leave it until the next day; and they should treat whatever is dewormed.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then resume the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the wound, as long as you see that it does not hurt any more at night; then treat the wound with ointment according to what is suitable, until it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the cauterization is held in fat, and the cope according to this form, long; and it burns your bones, and scorches all parts, and puts all your care for drawing out the poultice or the wound; and if the artery is made opposite, then do as I have said after this.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And if I make the cauterization when it is purulent, and cut and cure as I have said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cut is made after the cauterization when it is purulent and moist, if it is lighter, because there are few blood clots.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if at any of these cauterizations or burns or cuts there is no moisture, and these were the ones I made or were made by an old woman; and I found the cauterization like a sharp, rough, and bluish piercing, that could not be broken; and if none was made, it was as good as a wound like a piercing.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other cases, when an aposteme is present or chief, it is better that these which come as chief of the children and roots of the ears, the opening is made as soon as possible at the most dependent part of the ear, according to the size of the bowel; and they are cured as it is necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofuly
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times the aposteme is found at the collarbone, and the shoulder blades are dislocated, and the arms are broken, and never in any other part of the body, and they are mutilated and become unusable.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And every case of scrofuly is properly located on the side, just as the aposteme and chief are when they are present; and the appearances of these scrofuly are numerous.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	1. It has thicknesses that contain moisture, and if they are malicious and will not obey nature.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	1. In the one that you see in good disposition at the wrist, and is similar to the color of the cold corse, and is quiet in every part and not rough as the cold cold nerve, nor to the artery nor to the conduit, nor is it rough; if it comes that you cut it with a razor, and burn it in every part, and are the two lips of the knee as the bones, if you have the skill, as we have said in apothegms of the chief; and the hand is small and small, and you are sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and are not rough with the spatula and the trench, that the hands do not crack, and do not see too early, that you do not cut more than you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you touch the vein or artery, and it does not let you over, then put vitrol beads in the wound or any powders that stick to blood, and close the wound; and leave it until the abscess is relieved and the wound is soothed, and begins to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And if the wound is not healed, then return to your vein as soon as you can; then wait until your index finger tells you if it does not show any small pimples, whether the thumb and nails.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if the wound is a large pimple at its root, then you must only cut out that pimple at its root, but leave the other end of the thread double strong, and leave it hanging without causing any harm; then apply the wound with soft cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then the cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you cover the entire wound, and then assemble the two lips of the wound, and hold it now, before there is any excess due to the size of the wound.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you understand how to cover the root of it, and draw it out, and cut it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those wounds that have superfluity, perforate them or make them open; and perforate them as the one mentioned, depending on the size, then apply dressings with ointment and similar things, if it prevents further corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, if the cure of ointment makes it heal quickly, so that it is healthy.
de squinance	Of the skull
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and talked about the size of the neck; but I have never seen anyone in our world who does this, and it is the writing of their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have squinting, it is necessary that the incision of the throat called "epiglottis" be avoided; and this cannot be helped by it, because all the veins and the humors of the male patient are in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the ears.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the hard gums, it is necessary to cut off the epiglottis to avoid death that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to cut off the epiglottis, it is necessary to cut it at three or four points, passing through the two circles, according to the size of the incision; and they should be covered with cartilage; and then it is possible to cut off the epiglottis without injuring the throat, and the wounds will be long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	When the masters are unable to manage, if it extends the jawbone all around the neck, then cut through the hair as much as possible until it reaches the cheek; and avoid the veins of the face, if you see nothing, and then cover the wound as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the broken bone that jumped from the leg that was broken, and due to the lack of voice; and leave the wound open with a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed, if you doubt the dislocation, assemble the two lips of the wound, and cover all the surface that is felt on the cartilage; then administer medicines that make the swelling decrease as much as possible until it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim advises that as long as the throat is completely covered and the patient is unconscious, and the surgeons are deemed dead, then the operation can proceed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Adonques, it is advised to leave the incision open as long as the poison of the disease has not passed, and it will pass in three days or four. Therefore, it is commanded to cut the wound and treat it, once it is treated. And I will tell you what I see.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I see that a young woman was cutting her throat and cut off a part of her eyelids, and I was called to cure her, but I found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discover the wound, and find the blood that came from it, and it was well that it did not lead to any vein or only to the throat, and it came out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried to the wound and cared for it as soon as it was healed; and it did not cause the maiden any harm, and she only returned to her position after speaking in a red voice; therefore I said that there is no pain in the trimming of the epigastrium.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This hernia is called "hernia of the throat," and it is large hernias of a pale color, and they are very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural and accidental; or natural has no engine.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	The accident occurs in two ways, one resembling a large muscle, and the other is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery; it is painful, and there is no way to overcome it except for a small force, and it proves and searches all the introducer: if you do it as I have thick muscles, and cannot in any way, if the cope, so as one copes with thick muscles, and takes all of its force, if it has not; and it is well done, and the cure as it should be, until it is perfectly healthy.

de l’estopement de la verge	2. of the end of the beard
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	3. No child is ever born without having a pustule in the beard, or if it is small, or if it is not full in its place.

de la circoncision	Of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a trivial matter like other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own will, and properly as for our children, it is the best work we can do, and the most gentle for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not call circumcision of their sons, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I want the largest part of the masters and doctors who performed circumcision in the old days, and had forces, and at every age; if it were not for the fact that he had two hands, and by chance if he could not perform this operation and another one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	1. If the bone heals, and there is double pain, and the circumcision is not securely fixed to the point of the member; and if the circumcision of the finger is by chance cut off, it causes bleeding, and many times are born without any means of circumcision, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	2. Of the circumcision made with force, I have found the benefit of the experiment, because the forces cut both sides equally well, whether up or down.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	3. li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope. dou retenement de l’urine	The second line of the text translates to: "Hold back the urine.

des maladies de la vessie	Of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are itches or pains in the bladder, or when dysentery occurs and you see waters and medicines distilling, then do this to all the instrument called "cleansing", and it is shaped like this:

Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If it does not dislocate, make the patient lie on his back and put his hand on his side without hurting; then take the other hand, and squeeze the joint with the juice of a plantain or an algafer wine with vinegar, and massage the area.

de l’enfantement	of childbirth
