Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Then comes the form of the compress, which is placed on the wrists; and as the head turns, the joints turn as well.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Indeed, the corners should be more subtle and restrictive, and should be made of flat or curved wood; and the mouth should be no wider than the diameter of the thumb, and the margin of the branches should be no longer than a palm and a half, and no shorter than a quarter of a palm or a little more; and these two holes should be bored in the mouth of the shoulder to open when turning the corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, of a more subtle and lighter appearance, can be made of flat boards or sticks, according to the appearance of the nails; and it has two edges, as you see, like a palm of the hand, and they are wide; and when you open the marrow with all the instruments, if you place the woman's head on the bed, the legs and thighs, then adjust the tenails together in the marrow, and hold the instrument's handle steady between your fingers; then operate your hand on all the instruments, as you have done with the nails evenly, according to the quantity you see open the mouth of the marrow, until it fits as it was.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is used for every purpose and has many appearances; when it appears to the patient, the more hurriedly it is operated, and the higher the cost per quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument because you have not appeared to the patient, for their needs are not easily satisfied.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second child is retained in the womb, if you command the midwife to remove what the woman is holding, and then it is torn from the body, and her hands are forced to the mouth and nose; and if she jumps for this, well done.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, then if I can, and make a poultice or compresses, and put herbs that may open the mouth of the miscarriage, such as mint, rose, anise, chamomile, calamus, and centaury; all these herbs, or none of them, are cooked or can be boiled over fire; then put a cloth or compress, and the other end in the mouth of the miscarriage, and hold it until the vapors come out of the mouth; then make it wet, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second sentence is not understood, then.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	If the patient remains after this cure, and does not improve, then order the midwife to take her left hand in oil of mustard or musk, and then to push, and to want the second one; and when she finds it, press and stretch a little on both sides, so that the mouth does not resist during extraction; but it is necessary to move lightly to the right and left, and then pull; if it comes out and is healthy.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	The patient's mouth is dry and parched, so we recommend the remedy of sucking and fumigation with herbs; and if this does not relieve all that we have said, then you must follow our advice; but what is in the patient's mouth, tie it to the woman's navel, then cleanse it with a four-drug ointment; if it becomes raw and is replaced, and heals, then all will be well; but if it becomes rough and causes bad odor in the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is necessary to use fumigations, then none of the ancients have experienced fumigation of cress and dry figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument is such that it causes the woman to retain the flow and the second child if this is:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it seems like a cat, and it is placed subtly in the nature, and the large heads above the fire; and it is the fumigations from the charcoal, and the tanning as it is gnawed, and it returns another one.
de percier lou fondement	to break the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And many children are born who have not broken the foundation, but the child has swallowed something subtle and slippery: if it comes to the point that he perceals this slippery thing at his time, and does not perceal with a stone or a spatula, and gently takes the place of the ointment that it is not touched; then put on finely ground in wine and oil, and the cure of ointment as soon as it is healthy.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not remain, if you put or cut a nail in the toe, and leave it hands free, and be careful when you see the child coming to rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Neither does this cautery ever come out of a wound or abscess; if it comes, if you treat it, if as we have said, the toe nail.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula with great foundation.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the foundation are nodulation, and grow, as those that come from the ends of the second part, if there is one or more; and when this nodulation is old, it becomes active, and becomes rough or subtle in the blood or subcutaneous fat, and never are these fistulas permanent; they are known by the fact that they are caused by evacuation or ventosity when the patient evacuates, and by chance some fall.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	If there are fistulas that open into the bladder, and into half of the vagina; and they reach the junction of the thigh and the knee, and into the bone.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	If you want to know if the fistula is deep or superficial, and if it has any knots or turns, then use a thin wire of iron or silver in the fistula when it is not tortuous.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	If there are turns, then use a small tent or horse hair in the fistula as much as you can feel it with your thumb; and if you cannot feel it, and there is no egestion, wind, or water coming out, then as we have said: it is not perforated; if you hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	When the fistula is perceived in the bladder or led by the urine, if it jumps and cannot be soothed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perceived at the joint of the thigh, if it leads to the limb; if it has not tortuosity and the invention of pain, if it causes vomiting and there is no medicine to soothe by friction; and in these fistulas, there is no cure except labor and vanity of those who intermingle in them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not perceived and is ancient, there is hope for health through fire, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient's pain comes between your hands on his back; and he gently lies down on his legs until they are inclined to his belly; then cut a tent of rain, or a pillow if it has tortuosity, as long as you feel or the patient's tension comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	1. If the patient feels pain at the base, then it is likely that the joint is dislocated; and if you can discover or feel between your thumb and index finger, then it is suspected that the joint has dislocated; and you should check if it is properly aligned. If not, it cannot be treated.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	2. It is not possible to heal all wounds, but this is rare; and if you can help, then it is done as follows: if the fire cautery is subtle according to the size of the fistula, as said before; and the patient should be pulled through the fistula as soon as it starts to leave the base; and do this twice or three times, as you check that these charsets are straight, which resemble a penny's feather; then the dressing of soft cloths is applied, as long as the charsets are in place, then the ointment is applied, smeared on the charsets.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is in good health, so be it.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is not in good health, so be it. If the patient tries to force it, and cannot pierce it, and enters through the eye and into the brain, and sees a fistula formed at this point that covers the covering; if the cautery begins at the beginning of the fistula, and continues until the head of the tent, and then the cauterization is performed, as long as it remains at the end of the tent; then the tent will be delivered, and will remain; then the charred parts that seem like a feather's tip will disappear, and none will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	If it does not harm you, and cuts between you and the wound, whether by fire cauterization or medical boiling.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For fire cauterization has two effects: it knows the surety of these burned things, and the stoppage of blood and the removal of moisture; then the care of soft tents embroidered in burr or in cloth braided, as long as they gutter down, and the char remains in the wound; then cure the plague of soaked things enjanned with dry char, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healthy and does not return often.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	If a fistula comes suddenly with great force, and it is moved away from the body, if the throat is hurt or not, investigate this.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and if it is the skin or flesh, or charcoal, if it is only a sign of hope and expectation, by the administration of one of the three ways: if you cauterize as we have said, or if you cut it gently, or if you let it heal naturally and treat it as we have done; and do not move too much in front, so that you do not cut the tissue that holds the foundation, and wait for the discharge through the desired sense; then the cure, as we have said; by chance, if it is healthy, or you remove the covering and the mundane when it is healed from the foundation, or by tent or another instrument appointed; then mend the char that is in the wound as much as you can; then study to restore the wound and make the fistula longer in the part defended by the foundation: if it is still a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And no time are fistulas made in this way: and when you reach the end of the fistula, it is either costive or loose, if you take a tent according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I thrust it into the second, and thrust the tent all along the fistula as long as it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it persists in the edge of the loose flesh, then withdraw the thread from that pouch; and cut off the end of the thread, and assemble the two ends, and pull them apart, and leave one or both; and do not restrain it ever, as long as the threads hook onto those parts that are between two, and catch; then cure the wound as much as it is sore and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perceive, if you try to feel in all ways that you can, it should not be too difficult.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not necessary to make the plaster cover too much, and then the cure, as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny thistle whose fistula is made if it is too long and narrow, and on the other hand, because one cannot cope with it or must not cope with it, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of emorroydes
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	There are emorroydes in two ways: either they are made from the foundation, like resin grains, and they become smaller and larger, and then they are cut into sauces, and they become one or more, and they are defuer the foundation and at its head; but those that are defuer have little moisture, and they are cut into a small amount of quinque citrine or a small amount of wine, and they have the color of corsage; and the cure for those who have made the foundation defuer is that you command the midwife to ooze in chambers as much as the foundations become firmer, and the children appear; if you hurry, and you can handle them with your fingers, or you keep them in your nails, then cut at their roots; and if the uncine cannot hold them by their moisture, then tie them to the fold, or to the cloth, or to a piece of camomile; and you pull out the children, then cut, and powder some hot powders that are in the cautery leu; or you cauterize as it is said in the cautery chapitre, and the other cures as much as it is healthy; and if the foundations cannot issue, then clisterize the midwife with a clister tooth and sharp, and wash what is at the foundation, so that it may issue openly; if the midwife's mouth is not preint, and the children are firmer at the foundation, then the lightest cure is; and if you preign them with your nails or fingers, and cut, then cure as we have said, and as much as it is healthy, and without fear of incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it comes that you want to sew according to this manner: take one thread, thread it through an eyelet, and then pull the thread tight and make sure the eyelet is on the other side, and turn the two ends of the other thread through the eyelet, and if it is too large; and then tighten the thread, then knot the eyelet, and do this to all the others, and leave the corner excess of the suture; then put the wet thread on oil or rosewater at the foundation, and put the foundation, and command the patient to lie down; and then let it alone until it is dry, and when it is dry, if the cure of ointment and other cures are needed, as long as it is healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	The first sentence to translate is "dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement." In English, this translates
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there have been dry feces in the intestines, and by constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it comes to the point of a spatula or your nail scratching the wound, which does not allow it to get moist; then treat it as much as possible until it is soaked; and if it cannot be soaked, then repeat the scraping more forcefully than before, until it is clean and burned; then treat it as much as possible until it is healthy.
dou fremit	The first sentence to translate is "dou
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small appearance that should be cut from the chest, and it moves freely; and never does the knife touch it, and it feels like death to the chest, and it comes throughout the chest, and more hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that if you take a needle of a goose's throat, or a strong vulture's beak, and place it on the pulse, as long as the purple circle encircles the pulse entirely; then turn your hand around all the needle as you cover the entire pulse, and place it flat, and extract the pulse from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, if I make this of a goose's wing or of iron in this form, and is subtle and thin and well-cut:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not forget, but hold it with the other hand, and press. And if you see, if you cauterize the pulse, as it is in front or in the chapter of cauterization:
de la forme dou clistere	Of the form of the fire cautery
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never is it done that a silver or arch clistery, or an alloyed or polished one, is made; and never is it done that these are made of these strigils, according to which they are kept.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	For this reason, those that are used in the care of children and the weak and painful are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the fire clistery is small and large if it is used wide, or the belly is lined in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if it has a dislocation or the belly is lined in this way: and the head of the shoulder is dislocated, and in the other the arm, and so on; and the belly or puts the medicines in a beast's vessel or a linen bag, and feels all around each pertus, and between each pertus there must be a spice, then tie it with the thread in the pertus as strong as possible, and gather the belly like a stomach; and when the medicine is given, if the head of the shoulder is at the end of a strong thread, then cauterize; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	1. And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil or unguent of oak bark, or something similar, then lightly touch it; then the physician mixes his two hands together as much as possible, until it is all done, then remove the cloth, and gently lift the patient's legs to the side, and if the medicine comes out, as much as it can; and if the patient sleeps a whole night, it will be more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. And if you dislocate the hip due to disease of the abdominal wall, and the physician's medicine comes out, if it recurs as soon as it is safe.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the swelling is or foundation, or gangrene, whether the clyster is also subtle and as fine as with a child; and this is the form of the subtle clyster that is drawn when the skin is stretched.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said the treatment of wounds in the division of wounds; and you will say the treatments of hands and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the places where they are made, and how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things made by wounds are made of the edge of the cut, and size and depth, or lance or spike or spear, or similar things; or they are made according to the places of the body, as a wound that is made at the neck, or at the shoulder, or the chest, or the stomach, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will mention simple wounds on the shoulder, because the reminder will come in his chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or the bone is not broken, if it is from cutting or similar things, and the skin is torn and the wound is large, and you doubt slightly of hematoma chaut: if it becomes healthier of the head itself if there is little blood from the wound, and it should be healthier on the opposite part; and avoid the malady full of wine and fatty foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not become healthier, if the meat is anemic, and does not drink wine, and does not eat fat, and puts on the wound, it apostles with blood that is thin like oil or vinegar only; and if it does not apostle with blood, if it puts on the wound, it is fresh at all its sanc, and it is not moved by the air, dust, which I will say a little later; and if it has moved, if it puts on some ointments, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a spearhead and its surroundings, and the lips cannot be reassembled by tents, if they can be reassembled by stitching, like I will say for belly wounds, by sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone, it can be seen, and holds only by a piece of cloth; then cure the wound with medicine, restore it with leather in the skin, and order the patient to eat large meats, such as testes and cooked flour, as well as chicken, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you trueve or leather for food, and it does not reach the bone, then the whole porridge is lost, and becomes sour, then cure it; and if artere is in the wound or gut, which cannot be cut without causing pain, and it cannot be relieved by medicines, if one wants to cut the artery, and you trueve slowly, if the string is loose; and if this does not help, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	If these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and it is that you place in this powder which is always damp when the art has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take a part of incense; mix with three parts of dragon's blood; add three parts of live chalz, and the fine powder, and place it on the wound, and draw it out as much as it adheres to all its sanguineous parts; then close it well, and leave it to dry, so that it does not run or bleed, because the medicine is not effective until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And no time is made for a cauterization alone, when there is no candle or holy water from the dragon, but the surgeon has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the surgeon has moved the wound, then in this case, do not use any powder; but use some digested ointments or flour made from wheat and honey, until it bowes; then apply other cures as long as it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then use fine tweezers to remove it; and I will tell you more about this later in the case of deep wounds.
de la plaie dou col	Of the wound of the shoulder
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	A wound comes from the shoulder and it is simple, unless there is a difference between the two, but if the shoulder is the affected part or the artery is compressed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the shoulder that is affected, and there is no other option but to leave the treatment alone and not restrict anything, as it causes pain and draws back; and do not put anything on the wound, as the substance of the nerves is cold, and continuation with the brain, which is the more sensitive member; but if the medicine is suitable, like calm water rinsed with oil rose, and cleansed again in calm water, and other herbs according to this method, and moistened ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, if it is bound with bandages, then the cure as soon as it becomes healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are sore and full of blood, if it is bound with bandages as low as possible; and if the artery is cut, and discharge of blood comes, if it is treated, and the gauze, and cauterization is done as best as one can; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the jaw, and it is guided, as soon as the meat moves, if the jaw is cut near the neck, and it is repositioned according to its natural figure; then the extraction is done, and it leaves some jaws, then the care of dressings is given as soon as it becomes healthy; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, if you want; and if it has pieces of bone, if they are cut as small as possible, and those that you do not want to have, leave them as much as the wound presses, and so that it is dry and alived the issue; and if the wound is fresh, if powder is put on the powder I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If it has an abscess in the wound and if it has been drained, then the treatment is as I have described in this chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of the arrow or of the nail
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from an arrow or nail, and the wound is gushing blood, then look at whether the wound is mortal; if it is, then treat it as a mortal wound. If it is not mortal, and it is fresh at all its sutures, then do not put anything in the first hour, but let the wound be open and observe the patient; but if there is any poison, apply an attractive ointment, and touch the wound twice a day. If you have no ointment, put cotton in the wound to dry out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound three or four days, or more, until there is no spasm or trembling of the chest from the wound; if you see the bones in good position, then consider the wound saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the wounds with remedies and other remedies, as long as they are healthy; and if they cannot be healed, perform operations with sharp tools that have been made; if the treatment is done correctly.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is a cut or a stab with a sword or a knife, and it is simple, or on the back, if the treatment is done by the person in front; if it is large, use poultices; and if it is small, use powder; and if it is infected, and the pieces are taken out, if the patient wants to, and if they cannot be taken out, leave the wound open, and other wounds on other limbs are judged as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The first sentence to translate is "dou derrompement dou ventre". The translation is
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The first sentence to translate is "dou derrompement dou ventre". The translation is: "The dislocation of the stomach is great and deep, and often no intestines are injured; but there is usually an intestinal incision, and the abdomen is more swollen, and no small wound can be corrected as the large ones; for the intestines swell so much that they feel pain if they are put back in, and for this reason the moist plaies are most common, for the intestines are placed at the loins many times, and other wounds have fewer costures.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and there is no damage to the intestines, and it is easy to fix, this is one of the two methods: either by the size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is twisted due to the blow.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is twisted, handle it in this way: soften an sponge or a damp cloth only, or wet it with hot water, add vinegar and salt, and gently pull on the intestine until it unwinds; never force it, and it will come out easily.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	When you see the inflammation departing, if the intestine of acute or chronic and malnourished animals is cooked, it is because this is beneficial for the entry of a pocket of something; and if it cannot enter, then a pocket is made in the wound with the instrument of coi, and the first cure is to cut off the size, which is not necessary in great necessity and should not be; and this is the estrumens for the fendre: if it cuts densely in the corbeure and does not defuer, and sees the form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestine jumps, if it is put back according to its natural form in its own proper leu, you will have done well, because this is beneficial.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower abdominal region, if you intend to raise the patient's shoulder on his back, and raise his legs higher than his chest; and if it is in the lower abdominal region, then raise the chest and thighs higher than the surrounding areas, and thus the wound will be in one of the two parts as agreed upon, depending on which part is higher; and it is necessary to manage this in large and messy wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wound is small, and it is in the lower abdominal region, if you intend to raise the patient's shoulder on his back, and raise his legs higher than his chest; and if it is in the lower abdominal region, then raise the chest and thighs higher than the surrounding areas, and thus the wound will be in one of the two parts as agreed upon, depending on which part is higher; and it is necessary to manage this in large and messy wounds.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I arrived at the intestine and it had been 24 hours since it was injured, and the wound was 15 years old, and it was treated, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctor looked at the wound that was dying, and it was a miracle; and I did not use any ointment because there were no medicines in my legs where none were found, nor any remedies; and I washed more than twice a day with vinegar on the wound, and as soon as it became healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will tell me the two most common methods of sewing: take the needle, and thread it through the part that is deformed at the end of the string; when it has perceived the right angle in the right way, if the eye or the tip or the place where you have threaded the needle, and make it pass through another part of the deformed part; and the results of this sewing are that you will do it as the tailor does with the hair, and you leave once the thread from one part, and take it back again, until the sewing is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	1. The second method of sewing, which Galen calls his own, is the only one that anyone follows, which naturally assembles the two parts together, and applies one end of the thread to the other in this manner: take a needle or thread tail close by, and percify that one, and leave the other thread tail; then turn the needle, and percify through the part that is closest to the edge of the cloth, as the other thread tail; then percify the one and the other through the part that is closest to the edge of the cloth, in the other threads that are on the other side; and this is the best way of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens say this word, and no one testifies to it, we must sew the belly to the arrowheads, or they have a thread in each; and it must be one thread on one part, and the other on the other, in the manner of those that are cracked; and when the rupture is near the belly, if it is more painful than others in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	They judge the wound by whether it is like other wounds: and if you press the fresh wound with all its pain, unless the arse has moved, then reinsert the intestine and the bowels; then put some powdered charcoal on it, and if the arse has moved, then put any ointment that is present, as long as the wound is bloody; and cut the thread, and be sure to cut through the suture, and the mirrors; then cure the wound as you would with others, until it is healthy; and if you have no medicines, then use them, as long as they cause the bowels to grit, and mix it with vinegar, and stir it twice in the belly until it is healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not have other medicine in addition to these wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not become infected as the main members, then it comes that you lightly oil with ointment of tamarind or rose oil, and put on bandages, and dress the wounds; and if there is pain or swelling in the belly, and often it happens, if the clysterize with red wine, and at the same time the swelling comes to the intestine; and the percussed, and sauces that when it is the large intestines, it is lighter to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "young" cannot heal until it is unwound, and this is due to the tightness of the veins that it contains, and the subtlety of the entire body, and its proximity to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the gouge jumps from the wound, and it is reset as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is large and turns black, and you see the black leu, which is not alive, because it has veins and arteries; then cut what is in the ligament, and put the heads down until the extraction is ready for the gouge to bow, and the wound to bend.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured and the wound is small, if it can be restored with a few stitches, because I have seen that some were healed or the belly of a lance; and it was the wound on the left side of the stomach, and it was infected and became a fistula, and in it was the egestion and the vomiting; I treated according to what I could, and did not stop refining until it was healed, and I knew that it was healed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it closed, I doubted that the patient had no harm in his belly; but he had none, but delayed in better dispositions, and drank and ate; and they told me no surgeons that when a small wound is made in the intestine, one must close it in this way: take large thumbs, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the thumb has overstretched the mouth, if you put it between the lips, if it draws the mouth back; then close the thumb, and hold it so that it cannot slip, and then make another thrust in the same way as before, until the wound is entirely closed. Then close the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit. de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of a fistula or if it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	It is said that all wounds and abscesses, when they heal, if they are called universally "fistula", and moreover, if they are fine and straight.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the belief of the nodation that it must be hard and throbbing, if one feels pain, and is as fine as the tail of an ostrich; and never in a clear leap, and sometimes more; never thin, and sometimes thick; never short, and sometimes long; and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not cured, and does not hurt, is only due to one of the eight causes: it is to know, by the slight pain or corse; or by malice; or because the pain is too deep, and touches the lips, which does not leave pain; or there are too many boils; or the lesion is porous, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is like a pestilence; or because the property in the region is slow digestion, and slow health, and runs by nature; or there are wounds or holes: and I have shown all these causes and their signs and remedies with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	The first sentence to translate is: "Or covaint que je te faie a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par ouvre de main.

When fistulas appear in all the limbs of the body; for they have fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, nerves, or the small intestine, or the large intestine, or the bladder, or any of the ribs, or the spine's sharp end, or any joint of the hands or feet; and if a part of this principal limb is affected, and they resemble these.

The text describes the case of a young man who had a pain in his leg for a certain number of years, which was caused by congestion in his chest. dou feu	The first line of the text translates

de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
