Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	When the signs of the beginning of this vein are seen if it comes in the leg a very large inflammation, then it changes color, and begins to bleed, as if it were a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the wound is open, if it is necessary to cover it with a piece of cloth from one and a half inches to two and a half inches wide, and the edge, and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it is not closed, if the cloth covers the wound, and the edge; and if it is too long, if a part is cut off, and the remaining part is covered with the cloth, and does not cover its root, until it is all out; for if you cover it, it goes back into the body, and brings forth pus and blood or leu, and great disease; for this thing it is necessary that it be treated often and often, and nothing or no harm remains, and there is no time for this wound when it is treated with V paumes of long, or X, and some hands came to me, and it was X paumes long, and when you cover it, if blood or pus comes out, and the wound is perforated, so that all is out; and the matter that is densified, and applied to the leu with unjaundiced medicines porriture, no matter how much, then the cure is done as the apostemes.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And no time the hands are wet, and at the same time when it opens in the joint, whether the knee or the ankle, and a drop of blood comes out, and if it falls; cure the patient as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of those that are born between leather and skin.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our country "beef disease," because it often occurs in many cows, and is a small worm that passes between leather and skin, and goes up and down the entire body, and causes pain at every joint of the limb, as soon as it reaches the skin or rash, and jumps; and is caused by the excretion of some humors, such as snakes, worms, and scabies or belly; and one doubts its maliciousness, because when it goes up the body, it goes to the head, and enters the oil, by chance returns, and destroys the oil; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see the wound healing and drying, if it cannot be otherwise that when it will: if it comes to pass that you read the leg of the limb and its neighbor well closed, then close it and sew it, and it will stay in place, if the cauterization by fire is done as it should, until it is dead; and the greatest harm it can do, if it comes to pass that it touches the oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming towards the oil, if it is drawn away from it the corners of the lip will form, then close it and sew it; and it must use the cauterant with mundification of drug solutions for the human humors, and beware of animal fats as food.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from wind
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "wandering" pain, and is a pain that comes in various parts of the body, and spreads from one part to another; and I see what I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called a female patient, and I saw my arm, and I saw a small flesh in the vein of the shoulder; and after a little while, I saw it rise as if it were a wire from the shoulder, more quickly than anything else, as if silver were being cut from one part to another; the pain left that shoulder and moved to the shoulder, and then it spread throughout the body, so that it came to the other arm; then she told me that she dislocated, just like I see.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I am surprised to see how it moves from limb to limb, as I have never wanted this disease to happen in this way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I wished that people would not want to move the pain from one part of the body to another, but I do not want it, as I see in women; and I thought that this was because the woman had dry breasts, and the veins were discovered, and because there appeared that constraint; and I did not know until now that this is because of those who are delicate, and have moist breasts and veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	When you see the patient being cured of this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, if the limbs and toes are flexible, and then hold it as long as the constraint forces the leg to stay; and cauterize the leg; and if you do not see with your eyes the limbs, if the cure of this which relieves the constraint of the limbs, if like pills of herbs, and pills of hemp, and similar things.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the corps they enter.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of wounds is when there are those with large points, and small, and hairy, and sweaty; and those with sharp angles, and narrow ones, and those with long ones, and those with pieces; and one that goes into any member in different ways: or in the principal member, such as hair in the head, chest, liver, spleen, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	If the wound is in any of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you later appears, then you know that it is better to leave the extraction of this arrow than to die in many other ways; and if the sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not in front, then cut it out and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	1. When the sign of a fractured bone is seen when the limb is dislocated and pierces the bone, and the head of the cervical vertebra is forced into the eye socket, it is due to scotomie and sode, esvertin, and roujor of the eyelids, and inflammation and roujor of the tongue, and spasme and permixtion of understanding, and vomits of the throat; and by chance it may be due to nostrils or ears; and by chance it may affect the speech and voice; and a sudden jump of the white, moist wound-like incision resembles snares; and if you see this sign, if you seek treatment, and remove the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the shoulder when it is tense or painful is that it hurts or feels stiff near the left breast, and it seems as if it is becoming hard; by chance the shoulder also becomes cold, and there comes a chill and shivering, and shakes: then one begins to doubt that the patient is dying.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arm that is swollen is that there are no signs of scars on the wound, and the throat is swollen, and the face turns pale, and it sighs loudly and cries with pain in the heart.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the shoulder is dislocated in the covering of the chest, it is a great cause for concern and great pain and suffocation; and all the members of the arm are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the shoulder is dislocated in the stomach or intestines by chance, it is a fortunate thing that no food is affected;
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the shoulder is dislocated in the belly or intestines by chance, and it does not hope for the cure, nor the extraction of the arrow;
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the shoulder is dislocated in the bladder or urine by chance, and it comes out suddenly with pain and the patient feels great pain: fatal wounds are suspected.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, if the face, neck, shoulder, spine, helper arm, and spinal column are involved, is not considered as severe as before.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the artery is in the bone or the wound, and it is not pulsating, as I will tell you if I remember, because you are doing this.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I have heard of one case where the artery was cut or severed at the root of the nose: I tried to repair it, and the grease from the ear helped to save it.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I have seen a case where the artery was cut in the grease of the oil of the paper, and the wound was closed, and it did not reach the end of the finger, and it was as large as a Turkish bow, all without making the finger heavy with ears; the joint was saved, and there were no accidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And there was a gash in the throat of a man, and it was the Arabian scar on the ears: I was the beard, and subtle as I passed, and it was safe for the crests.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And there was a gash in the man's belly, which I thought was fatal; and then after XXX years, if it did not change its position, I opened the gash, sutured it, and reset it, and there were no further complications.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if a man has a gash in the back or belly, and it is the wound that was sutured; and the gash did not heal quickly, and did not change its natural dispositions, and did not find any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man, who struck a thorn in his face, and felt the wound; and it took a long time to suffer great pain; and of other similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And found a thorn in the shoe of the king, who had it stuck in his sole and was slightly deformed on the right side; and the thorn was completely embedded after three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound to be very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried to remove it with all my subtlety, and I did not feel anything; but I felt a sharp and painful sensation in my right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow I placed my hand on the affected limb, because I didn't feel any pain; but I realized it was from the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice to my hand, and the right side of the wound was relieved, and it delayed the patient's pain for a long time, until he felt the arrow in his shoulder; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied the poultice to the wound with my hands, and as it was overturned, I pulled it out, and felt the head of the arrow in my shoulder; then I added more medicine to the wound through that arrow, until the patient's pain became visible; and it took about four months to heal, and then I removed the nails, and the skin from both sides, and could not; therefore I continued to refine and invent ways to strengthen, as soon as I had well-made nails, according to how the form will come in this chapter, as soon as I treat the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the patient thinks that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it therefore, and it was sutured to the wound, and the patient became healthy entirely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have said the quality of extracting some arrows, if you put your cure on what I do not tell you, because the books cannot make everything look beautiful; but the masters of the things most important and present, use nine different operations and nine instruments, in descending the things that are drawn out in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows do not come from the limbs or they are false if according to two ways: either by the leg or they enter, or otherwise; and the one that is thrown by the hand or it enters, is an arrow that has entered into the flesh, and it will never be thrown again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if she does not jump now, if she leaves it until the hair is completely dry and the skin is pale, and then she lies down in the bone, and she cannot get up if she does not have any strength left, and no movement at all, and then she jumps, and if she does not jump, if she perceives clearly at any point, as long as the skin is pale, and then she will be weak.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrowhead is lodged in the bone, and it will go to one of the stomachs, and any of the accidents I have mentioned to the helper: if he does not remove it, but leaves it as long as it is even after some time, because if the arrowhead goes to one of the stomachs, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	When the dislocation is only in the bone and does not cause facial pain, and there are no other unusual occurrences, it is not a serious matter for the surgeon.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation worsens and cannot be fixed, then immediately call for help; as I have said, and then treat the limb until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the dislocation cannot be seen in the limb, and you want to try everything; and if you feel it, if there is no instrument that can be used for reduction; and if you do not have any pain or swelling, but the joint is very large; then reduce the joint as much as the wound allows, and if the joint has ears that hold it, then apply pressure on the ears of the joint with your hand, and then break or squeeze the ears of the joint as much as you can, and carefully, even though you may have broken the joint, continue to treat it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not once, if the bone is still alive and wet, then cut it, for the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the dislocation does not move in the direction of the bone, then it is against what we have said in this chapter; and you should make an incision on the nerve and vein, and insert a thread as you think you can most easily draw out the arrow, whether it is sharp, or blunt, or closed, or open; and place the needle according to the form of the hole that the arrow made, for this is the greatest help that can be given, and if you do not, if you do not, then follow what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The first line of the text translates to: "The arrow that comes from another part, or it opens no thing of him, or his skin is wrinkled in some place so that one can see or feel it: then take it out, as much as the nails can hold, and then pull it out: if it hurts now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, if you turn your round hand around as much as it enters the bone, and widens the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be pulled out, if you leave it alone, and then resume the extraction as much as it can be pulled out; and if it is a sore, and you see that it is bleeding, if the instrument points to the hair of the instrument, and then pull it out, and if the sore is hair, and the instrument point enters it, for lighter extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrowhead is fully inserted, then you should cut through the entire shaft or remove it as soon as possible, and then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the arrowhead is stuck in the chest, abdomen, or intestines, and it has protruded, then you should quickly cover it with a piece of cloth, and then remove it along with the nerve and the wound. Then treat the wound as needed, and keep treating until it heals completely.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tines used to remove arrows is similar to the beak of an owl, and it looks like this:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they are of different ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.

des sainies de ventouse	Of wounds from ventouse
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Wounds from ventouses are made of horn, or iron, or silver; and ventosations are made in two ways: either by cutting and drawing out blood, or by cutting without causing bleeding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez. Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And if those who are in health are cold-blooded and too hot and inflamed, then it comes that they need to eat things that are cold, such as pomegranates, endives, and leeks, and similar things; and they need to drink milk, and charred meat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with cold complexion, if they crave honey syrup, and sweet wine odorant moien, which is between viel and noveil, and drink little, and drink poc, and pucins and small oiselz and pijons; and when they start to vomit, it must drink more than mengier; and it is necessary to give some men once triaicle or muscate before the ventosacion, or after, to comfort the principal members; and let them be subtle in the without, but only those who are chaut the boivent.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The stings that are made to hurt are those that are made in the liver, and in the spleen, and gout, and in the stomach and bowels and intestines and bladder, for this member does not suffer much hurt outside, and only causes pain when it attracts sanc from member to member, as we do with the mameles when they are not sainne; to remove the viscositeit that is in the member, as we do with the stomach and bowels to anmenuisier the member; and to relieve the pain, when it has opilation or pierre, if it can attract the opilation by its virtue, or desert the pierre of his leu; and then it is made to ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, and these stings are administered empty to suck only; and never are administered together fire, and no plains of aigue tede, as in many diseases of pleuresin, and in such way we fill the sting with hot aigue soule, or with aigue that has been cooked herbs in it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the forceps administered by fire is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two palm-wide and half inches of parchment, and has one cost at the top of the little pus, like a needle, and is made of iron, and has a notch on the other side so that it does not hurt the patient when inserting it into the member; and in the middle, there is a groove of iron or of brass, to hold a thrusting needle, and in this there are large and small ones according to the diseases and the pain of those who take them; for the forceps of children are not like needles, nor thin like fat, but they are made of iron.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	The following line should be translated as: "And then put the vacuum tube on the member: take the cork or liniment, and insert it into the vacuum tube through the hole that is in the vacuum tube, so that it does not melt at the end of the vacuum tube; and then place it on the member, and your must be as we have said, if you see, if there is steam, and then you take the vacuum tube; and take the liniment as before, and repeat it often, if you have skill.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the vacuum that is maintained in a patient with pneumonia, there is no hole or perforation, and it is not infected unless it is only when it is clear of phlegm, and it is placed on the member only when it is; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without doubt, dislocations are not found except in joints where it is not possible to put a splint due to their small size, such as the lips and genitals, and similar parts; and in them, the bones are lacking in cartilage, and others are like this; and the quality of the user is that when you find dislocations that are in soft waters, if you take them; and put them in a soft water, as long as they are not pregnant, and have nothing in the belly; then it is healthy and cleansed, then wash the member as much as it is red, and put on the splint; and when they become flat and smooth, and turn white, if it is the leg or the arm, put it on, because this is afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then raise the leg of the affected side, and then the knee; and if the patient is too cold after the corset, then soak a piece of linen in cool water, and put it on, as long as the leg is cold; and if the leg is frozen, then put a piece of hot iron or glowing coals on it, and similar things, until it is warmed up; or you can half-peel the feet of wet leather, and leave them as they are on the foot, if it becomes warm now; and if you have more time, then take other frozen feet.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not take on the salve, if you rub the lew with fresh sanc, or thrust a needle as much as it will go, and then insert it, and as they feel the sanc, if they smart; and when you see that they seize, if you dust some aloe and flax, or charcoal, if they now burn.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the beginning of the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Ask, gentlemen, what the folk think of this chapter, that they see no use in it, and no ancient books or letters; and for this reason, science has been neglected in our country, because I have never found any book; and I know nothing, only that by the science of ancient books, or by my study and treatment of the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life, and I have described in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have summarized it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the strains that are cut, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say at the beginning of this book the sum of words and chapters or the surgeon puts his understanding, and studies the truth, so that those who have experienced it may know this noble art, and learn it for others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that if any fracture, dislocation, torsion, or twisting occurs to no one, if it comes to pass that you must cut off the flesh of the patient on both sides, without anything else being harmed, whether it be by forceps, catguts, or sutures; or if you hold him tightly and he is not very thin, nor too fat; and if his face is cold, it is to know that the cold joules, and the char of oak and horn, and he does not drink wine, nor eat raw meats, and does not fill his veins with blood, as long as you do not doubt of apoplexy coming, or expansion of matter in the member; if the patient's flesh returns to its former state, as it was under the same government as it had used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the bones begin to heal, if it is necessary to remove the patient's food, either because of large stools or because of viscosity, like bread cooked in wine, and tests, and pies, and pancakes made with wheat, fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the stool becomes less and the fracture is repaired sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And you advise that the bones broken and decayed cannot be well recovered or mended according to their nature by the care of the limbs, nor those who are too soft; but if it is necessary to break the bone and join the joints together as much as possible, then it should be done in the same way as before, and not allowed to go hungry for long periods of time, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	The treatises mention various types of fractures in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	However, the fracture of the head is different from that of the leg or arm, and I will tell you about all types of fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There are fractures that occur when struck, and others when grazed, like the size of a quill to write.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a small nick can cause a break.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each fracture has its own mechanism and instrument for restoration, according to the remembrance that comes to their mind; and the fracture of the bone is caused by the bone being twisted, and widely open by deformed, and some under pressure of the hand; and if it is not twisted or cut, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture, but it may have twisting, or nick, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you can only manage to move it with your hand, but take the medicine that comes after, and then try again gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then assess the fracture that will occur in the wound, and the two parts that are dislocated. It is now appropriate to stabilize them as evenly as possible, unless the patient becomes faint or dizzy; and if the patient becomes faint and passes out, until the faintness has passed, then it should be gently and wisely placed at the edge of the bed and the patient should be encouraged that the restoration of the dislocated part is lighter than the restoration of bones or pieces; then the patient is extracted, as it is appropriate to do after.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	When there are broken pieces in the bone of the foot, if they are two parts, it is hands or feet, or a part of your hand is small members, or two strings, or one string and your hand; and put the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are adjusted, if you adjust by your own means the additions in their place in the bone that you please, and keep that by your effort does not cause the surgeon's injury or pain; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And it feels good to the hand if it seems that it is not well: if it curves beautifully and is not strained too much, do not press as those who come by their own effort make the wound and contraction of the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	When the limb is at rest, if the patient carefully keeps it still, neither by day nor by night, nor when turning in bed, nor in any other way, then the limb should be firmly held so that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when there is no pain, if it is not yet at rest, and it is necessary to put the limb in its proper position so that it does not feel any pain; and you should hold it steady so that twisting does not occur when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I will tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Saws that the broken limbs are of different sizes in smallness and large size and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For if it has bitten members, as if they were twisted and similar: if it comes with rolled linen and fine threads; and those that are large, like a thick leg: if it comes with rolled wide and hard threads, for the wide bands encompass all the large member, and draws it evenly, unless it has no taich; then it lightly winds around the limbs three times or four according to the member, and draws the hand tightly along all the linen, then goes to the end of the fracture and draws it less, that the fracture can slightly move the part; and softens the linen a little by little, as much as you can reach a large part of the healthy limb, then take another linen, turn it over towards the broken part, and then return to the part opposite the fracture, and draw it gently, not too much nor too little, as we have said in the first step of the fracture; then put between the wounds of linen or threads, as they are equal, then tie all with a bendil, and then put your good stitches on, if it has not aposteme or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if it has been struck or infected, if he puts something soothing on the infected part and leaves it alone for some time; then he should tightly hold his eyes, and they should be of a width equal to one-third of a wide knife, or of a fist that is used for fighting, or of rains from palm trees, and they should be like this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the thing he puts on the wound is larger and broader than the others; and it should also be as long as it is necessary for the small or large member; then tightly hold the eyes as you did in the first part, then tie a thread around it as you did in the first part, but do not make it too tight, less is better; and the thread must be smooth, neither too thick nor too thin, and it should be of linen; for if the thread is too thick, like the works of the fools who make their laces with linen threads, it is a great error, because the wound cannot be even if it is too fine, and it can only be between each eye less than an inch wide.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is anesthetized by the heads of the pins after the extraction in healthy people, then they should be covered with linen or silk, if it does not cause pain.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the splint, and the bones are broken, I will tell you the treatment for this afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And be careful that it is not too tight on all the broken limbs at once.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not advisable to put on splints immediately, but rather after several hours or days, or according to the patient's strength; and this is the way the ancient emplausters were used to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that is ground as fine as flour from a molin, mix it with a lot of water, and make a dough with it, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way to restore fractures in other positions, and even in women and small children, because it is not too tight nor too harsh.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	1. Another way to mend fractures and dislocations and twists: take garlic, vinegar, oil of cinnamon, Arabian gum, and musk, in equal parts; mix with aloe, in equal parts; and make a powder, and mix with the fat of onions; if the complexion of the face is hot, use this ointment as it is of good composition and restores broken bones quickly and benefits many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	1. Another way to mend twists: take Arabian gum and vinegar, in equal parts; mix with aloe, in equal parts; acetic acid, in small amounts; arsenic, in large amounts; and cook well, and mix with vinegar or fat of onions, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Other ways to apply plasters to joints and bones, and alleviate the pain coming, and the wound uses of the bone, and the bandage: take new cloths, and the oil in a bowl and cooked, and put on the leg.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Other plasters do not heal, but it is necessary to alleviate inflammation and bone pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other ways to apply plasters that heal broken bones: take dry fig leaves, and earth oak leaves, and bind them together, and make the plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Other ways to apply plasters for healing of bone fractures and to reduce inflammation.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	1. Gather the roots of malva, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of violets, and each part in equal measure; and grind them, and mix with wine, and wash your limbs with cool water, or with cold water, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	2. Another way to emplaister more forcefully than the first, when the wound is deep and comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	3. Gather the roots of malva, and linseed meal, balsam, honey, and violet flowers and each part in equal measure; grind them, and mix with cool water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the chalor of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In the book of Ypocras, it is stated that nothing is used to set a broken bone for restoration, except for wax and oil, and no other thing is used. And he said that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It seems that Galen says that to set a broken bone for restoration, one should use dry, hot things, such as mirrors and aloes, and incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to describe the value of a wound and pain: take a knife and needles made of hooves, or feathers, and vismalve, and seil igalment, and the broie, and make an application and put it on the limb.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the patient will feel better in a short while, and if there is no pain in the joint or the bones of the limb, and if there is inflammation or itching, and you hurry to remove it, and apply the plaster now; then gently dampen a cloth, soak it in sea water, dip it in cold water, and lift the limb until the itching stops and the pain subsides; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, moisten it with cold or olive oil, and tie it up, as long as you are sure not to have gangrene; then allow the inflammation in the member to subside and the pain to disappear, and then resume the application of the plaster lightly, a little at a time, and do not strain it too much; and gradually until it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the wound is swollen, bleeding, and painful, and it has become inflamed, then you have the skill to plaster and bandage, if it recurs, as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If you do not see any sign of what we have said, if it does not come to the member for three, four, seven, or ten days; and never more than twenty days, as long as the fracture is healing and approaches the bone; then the restraint must be greater, and the tissue grows larger, as I have said before; and if you see the skin becoming harder than it should, watch for signs of infection; apply warm tea to the member every time you see it, and do this every hour, and also use a cloth to cover the member; through this process, you will cut off the infection at the member, and mend whatever damage was done to the flesh, so that the member returns to its normal state: this is good, and if it is done correctly, there will be no more pain or discomfort.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of wounding
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many kinds of wounds, and various shapes; for there are wounds made by the blow of a spear, and which pierce the bone all the way through to the other side, as if it were hazel or ivory; and therefore this kind of wound is called "hazel" wound.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the spear strikes the bone in different directions and is called this kind of wound "absolute"; and these are the wounds of these two large or small gashes.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is a percussion, or a thrust, or a piercing, or a cut through the pierce, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a constant fracture, which draws close the skin that is loose from the bone, or it is under the bone, and this wound or large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	If a wound that is healed in the bone as well as under it, and is a small cut, and for this it is called the "capillary fracture"; and if the wound that is made by injury, or by piercing, or by something seeming, and lets the piece of the bone enter, and is the same size as when they were heated during the forging; if it enters through the piercing.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And then comes what happens underneath, which have either dry bones or wet ones like children; and they happen in all these ways of fracture that are light in pieces if they are like these; and I will speak of it in their language.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us see all ways of fractures by the method they have, and through inquiry, and by the corrupt char that is there.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hairy skin is known by what happens when one discovers the bone, and one rubs with the finger, if the dark fracture is not open.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, take care of the patient's condition, and if you see no accidents, it is like vomiting of bile, and admission, extension, and swelling, and fever, and the wound turning pink and red, and other signs that appear in various dispositions, if it cannot be cured with doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a dangerous accident, and you hope for a quick recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the bone comes first to you, and it is in the wrist, then it is necessary to treat the bone before the fourteenth day at the doctor's office that you should go.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in this way, then if you hurry to treat the bone before the ninth day, unless the bone has already become corrupted and the accident we mentioned comes.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture comes just before the wound closes, and it is necessary to cut off the broken part: and it is that you ignite the chief of the new wound, and uncover the bone in all the ways you can, and uncover the shape of the wound more so than you can, and if blood comes out to expose the bone, or gangrene occurs, then help yourself as you can, and it is that you fill the wound with oiled soft cloths; and let the wound rest until the gangrene is subsided and is secured from decay; then begin to treat the bone, and it is done according to two ways of dissection: one way if you cut at the narrow end in the shape of a form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I cut it in another, larger piece than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is if you have many different sizes, some thin and others wide, and they are sharp, and they are of iron; and you cut them lightly, so you do not cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and brittle, then you must perceive it by piercing with a needle, otherwise you must sharpen the edges with tweezers, not making them too thick that they do not pass over the bone; and you must have more of them, so that each time it happens in the joint of the bone, if you have tweezers for your test; and this is the form of the three ways of tweezers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality of perceiving through the broken bone is that you place your thumb on the bone, and turn it around as much as you can until you feel the bone is perceived; then put your thumb on another part a little later, and then do everything, and cut the incisions in the bone that are between the holes, and do it as subtly as you can, and gently, as we have said, as long as you trace the bone with your hand, or with any of the tweezers you have, like needles; and make sure you do not touch the brain or the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have perceived and cut the bone, if it covers the opening that the bone makes in the other instrument as an incision, but it should be smaller and more subtle than the other incision; and if it does not cover any small bones, nor any scales, if the light bones are gently with the tweezers; then cure the wound with tents and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of opening is when it is done by the Galians, who are more skilled; and the hardest, and that is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to remove a part of the bone, where the fracture is open and visible, so that once you have removed this part, measure from the top of this incision, the curve of this lenticular incision, which is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut too much, and the part that is cut should be in two layers, if the cutting is towards the bone; then with a small nail, if you lightly touch the bone all around, and keep well guard of the cloth that is on it; if it is near the bone, as the bone is sensitive, and is felt with pain, and is feared.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only crushed by the hands, and it has small pieces, then cover those sharp edges with something, and file down the scales using a subtle raser, of which you must have several quantities to meet the needs of each limb according to the extent of the fracture and its appearance.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you sharpen before with great rasers, and then with more subtle ones, and continue doing this as much as it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In every other hair cutting and subtle fracture, it is necessary to meet the needs according to its direction; and this is something that cannot be denied to the one who has studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	When the scar is discovered, if it is necessary to apply linen to the wound according to its size, and mixed with oil of rosemary, and placed on the wound; then take another doubled bandage of II or III, and mixed with wine and oil of rosemary, and placed over the first bandage; and apply it more gently than you would, so as not to burn the scar, then dress with other linen, and do not strain it too much, only as much as it adheres to the wound; and leave it for II or III days, until the swelling is subsided, then remove it, and apply medicines such as roots of lis, flour of times, powder of incense, aristolochum, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and place it on the wound, and apply other medicines without soreness; and when the wound is clean, do not leave the ointment or assemble bowels, for if bowels assemble under the skin, they can cause great harm to the patient; for if something malicious is placed on the scar, it can cause pain.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	When a patient is about to undergo surgery, if no accidents have occurred in the past, and as we have said, if there is any doubt, then it is not certain what will happen.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no pain is felt during the surgery, and it is only due to the medicine that has been given, then if a part of honey is ingested along with three parts of rose oil and one drop of glue, and it is mixed with water, then the cure can be applied in various ways until the patient is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Wounds that are never broken are the two bones that are often injured, or only one, because they are two bones; and this is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it becomes healthy.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should cut off your small did or pertuss and place it equally on your index finger, and in the pouch until it returns to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and let the patient feel no pain through your touch.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part of the nail, and cannot be brought to the root, then you should place it equally at the base of a large nail.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, then you should re-do it and restore the first joint, if possible; if not, after the second or third time, when the inflammation has subsided, then cut off the nail at the base, using scissors, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If you cut at another part, it will be; and let the wounds be as large as they fill the cavities.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And no restorer would say that one must smooth the wounds in burrs, and each one would die.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It seems to me that it is well, but the wounds must be smoothed in the making of oven ashes and powdered mill; then leave the wound, as long as the bone is hard, and the cartilage is firm.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And no time is it cut on the neck of the wound, and if it is soft and draped, and holds the bridle, and blows the salve among; or do as you have seen.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if you have a wound, the cauterizing iron comes to the affected part while you are working, and if it is placed with fine thread or silk soaked in rose oil, or in the mouth of a vial.
