Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you have a wound, the cauterizing iron does not come to the affected part, and if it is placed with plaster made of flour of barley and incense powder, mixed with egg butter, then it is covered with light sponge pieces, and the wound is not closed; and if the wound is small, and it is torn into small pieces, if the stitches are comfortable for this, then cut the thread, and the cure of things strangely shaped is sown, and sewn, as with plasters and ointments suitable for this; and if there is no wound on the skin, the wound is cured by bandages, and it is stitched with needles as much as necessary to make it healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the dislocation of the lower jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is dislocated, there is no wound, and the fracture is not severe, but only slightly so, and it is not broken into several pieces, but rather a single piece that can be bent slightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary to note that if the fracture is on the right side of the jaw, you should place your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left side of the jaw, you should place your index finger on the left hand, gently bend the fracture, and then hold it with the other hand to prevent further damage.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the lower jaw is described as II, then it is necessary to administer an extension of II parts, as long as they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth move, or fracture, then the patient should use a gold, silver, or silk thread to secure the broken lower jaw to the dislocated part, and then place a large staple or piece of leather along and across the jaw, and fasten it to the muscle that is being used, and instruct the patient to rest, and provide light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, and if it moves to another point, and then return it to its original position; and apply powder with a lot of urine or flour from the grain mill, after you have osteit the cerote; and apply light emplaustre, and when it is set, and the disposition of the malaide does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy; several times it is healthy in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	If the abscess ruptures, then it is best to follow what we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If there is a fracture and wound combined, the piece of bone that is exposed is a flat piece of the bone; if the bones are subtle and flexible, they can be easily bent.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is wide, it should be widened according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have all the bones in place and there is no pain, if the wound is wide, make sure it is large and stitch it with flexible stitches to hold it together and heal.
de la forcele	Of the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks more often in front of, towards the shoulder, and the break is in three ways: either it is broken and dislocated in two, and it has pieces, and it is the lighter to restore; or it is broken with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the dislocation is when the break is felt as pain, that you have two assistants, if one of them touches the injured shoulder that feels the strength of the break; and the other extends the collar towards the part; then place the dislocation in your two hands, so that it forms as it should, and there should be no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you have further work to do, place the shoulder bone of the patient at a distance from the mallet with a round or flat bead of linen, or cloth, and make it as large as needed; then gently apply force and pull the bead towards your hand so that you can evenly close the fracture, just like we do.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you do not want to cut the head of the mallet with the force, because it comes off easily, then it may cause the mallet to turn in its socket, and place the shoulder bone at a distance from the eye, and pull the muscles of the shoulder away from the eye, as long as the head of the force remains raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture to your two bones, and if you find the fragments loose, then you must cut them off; and take care not to cut through the pieces too much, and if they cannot be joined by any means, it is likely that the tool has struck one of the incisors you have; but make sure to use the right force with this instrument to avoid damaging the face.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and is not too thick, and should be as wide as it appears to be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the will; and if there are any fragments, if you see them, and some are large, and others small, if they are the fragments of the fracture you made when you treated the bones; and if you feel aposteme chaut, if the wound is large, or you doubt aposteme chaut, if you use the wound with drapels and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if the abscess bursts and comes out, if it is filled with oil of rosemary and saffron and wine, it should be cleaned.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And the treatment of the bone is when it feels pain and seems too small, you should put the bone on a mill of fine powder of rosemary and saffron and wine, and light sponge on it, and a small hole in the wound; then take a very large palm leaf, then put the damp sponge on the sponges, and press; then take a fine needle of three to four inches long and long, and wrap around the braid, so that the end of the braid remains; then put the needle on the wrist, and turn the braid around the wrist, and soak the clean bone in unsalted oil, and soak the salty bone; and pull each part, and when you see that the braid holds the wrist well, and you can clearly see that the needle does not stick to the bone, if the reward is for each, and when it tightens, if the restraint; and make sure the mace on its back, and it puts when it goes to sleep a small pillow of oil on the wound, or lift the helper up; if the fracture is closed by the alignment of the shoulder or the arm at the shoulder, or you put the arm against the collar, and does not slip out of hand accidents do not come, just twenty days; then resume the pressing, if it seems to have merit, and pull it out and leave it as it is, until it is restored; and it is restored in the most 28 days, and less for any man.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the break of the elbow
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the elbow breaks or widens, and it does not fit well, and it cannot be put back in place; if the humerus follows the shape of the break, and the bone is reshaped according to its natural form, in all possible ways that you can; then take some powdered sulfur with a lot of urine, and light spices, and place a flexible plate larger than the elbow, and make sure it fits well on no part of the elbow, if you use a soft cheese cloth, so that the plate sits evenly; then tie it tightly with a rope or cord, so that the plate does not move from its place, and watch the line every time it loosens, and whenever it tightens, and moves the plate when it is free from the bone, and look at the pain on his chest; and the elbow is restored in 20 days or 25, and when those numbers are completed, if you leave him, and be sure, because only lightness is put in place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is found to be weakened beforehand, and it does not bend, if it is found, and the bone, and make what we have said in the breaking of the force of the painful abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is never broken in a million years, but this does not happen; but it often breaks in the winter.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in two, if it is not bent, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of strength, and all, and by chance vomiting blood, and open the chest in the broken bones, and it seems well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the patient's shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it cannot stay in place despite being reset repeatedly, first reset the dislocation. If the dislocation persists, it may be due to corrosion or pruritus that comes to the affected area, or pain or aposteme if there is any, then remove the plaster, and address whatever came from the methods of treatment. Then reapply the plaster as needed until it is in its proper place.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The symptoms of the rib fracture are that it only occurs after a great blow to the back and chest, and does not cause much pain in the investigation; it is well understood.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you wish to set the fracture, as it should be done.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then place the splint, and tighten it with a staple, if you have the skill.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is displaced towards the chest, it causes great pain and pressure, like giving birth; the chest does not fit well; they tie it, and then vomit large amounts of blood, and this is a sign of serious illness, and the ancients have often put a large bandage on it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	If it is said that it should be administered animals that inflame the stomach, by putting the bracelet on the shoe.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this mistake, that ashes do not come, if it has not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes, if it is good.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And none of them say that they put ventsouces on the shoulder, for sweetening, and it seems right; however, doubt is that the ventsouce does not attract the excess to the shoulder because of the position of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And none of them say that they should cover the shoulder with soft oiled gauze and put tents between the ribs to measure the hour accurately, then treat the pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure through the bone that pierces the tissue, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to cut into the shoulder blade where the rib is broken, and it is necessary to put on an instrument to hold the face; therefore, it must be fractured the bone, and it should be drawn lightly, and then the edges of the wound are sewn if they are large, and it is cured from plasters as long as it is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	2. If an abscess comes, if it is covered with soft ointment, and it is covered with cloth; and treat while the wound is coming out of the abscess, and it should be cleaned under the cost over where it needs to be, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure dou col	Of the wound of the shoulder
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a wound to the shoulder bone, and rarely does it happen; and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when you see it is not, and you know if it will be alive or not, if you see your hands soft and swollen and lifeless, and cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, if they do not feel.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	It is said that it is mortal in many positions, and if they are held still and feel well when extracted and not, it is said that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured, if it is put to proper care.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if such a thing comes to the spine of the back, and you see whether it is healthy or not, if you are careful to see if the bones are broken, and the accidents that are in the hands, and if the loins jump and there is egestion with will; and when it is sawn at its stomach, there is egestion with will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is sawn at its back and you see that it is boiling, if it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Says that it is mortal: if it does not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come, then it is the more lighter thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	1. If the patient is in pain due to the wound, if it is an abscess that has burst, then put on olive oil or oil of myrrh as much as possible; then put on a comfortable plaster and bandage, and tie it with a string, and tell the patient to rest; do not sleep more than that part of the body where the pain is felt, as long as it is healthy.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	2. If any bones break, then put on a bandage around the joint; then open the wound, if it is large, stitch it together with one stitch, then dress the wound with ointment, as much as possible; and if the bone is broken, which is called the "broken bone," take your left hand pouch from your right hand, and put it on the other hand at your foot, then put on the plaster and bandage, if you can; then pull it out, and if it has broken, then set it and treat the wound as much as possible.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the bone of the shinbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	There comes a time when the shinbone is fractured, and if it does, it is not usually a minor injury to the head; it becomes long, and slopes downwards, and pain comes to the leg, the knee, and the wound is swollen.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that if you extend your hand over it as long as you are on the fracture; examine what the fracture and its appearance are like; and if the fracture is only at the top, place it in natural position as much as possible.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	If the fracture is long or it declines towards the dens, then I advise the surgeon to operate on the patient's abdomen as long as the restoration of this fracture depends on you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	If you have placed it evenly, then place the plaster on it, then place a piece of wool or feather, and hold the fracture so that it does not move; and then apply the shoulder to the ribs, as long as the swelling is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If the abscess is opened and there is no pain, then as long as the abscess is not painful, put on the dressing we have mentioned before; and then return to the restoration, and hold it as it should be, if there is no other accident; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	The first sentence to translate is "de la brisure de l'ajutoire". The translation is "of
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The second sentence to translate is "Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, sekon ceste forme:". The translation is "The assistant is the one that is between the shoulder bone and the shoulder blade of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then you must restore it according to one of the following two methods: one of which is to take a piece of green gourd, in this form:".
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	The third sentence to translate is "Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en hup, et siece li malaide sur I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sur le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covante." The translation is "And the patient can move the limbs and sit up, and the surgeon sits on the seat; then the broken arm is placed on the fist, as it goes to the elbow, and has a crutch of the fist, then it can bear any heavy thing or extend the hand; then the surgeon places the brace in his hands together, as long as the brace returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is if one binds the patient to their horror, and holds their hand to their collar, then commands the ministers to mark the ones that are at the bracelet on their hands, and the others mark them differently everywhere they can, and extend each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more difficult, then pull the hands apart and stretch them as much as possible, and extend each of the ministers to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the bracelet is close to the shoulder blade, then it is necessary to make the hands moist and stretch them away from the shoulder; and if the bracelet is towards the elbow, then it is necessary to gently place the hands on the shoulder and elbow, as long as the bracelet is even with the shoulder and elbow, and then tighten the bracelet as much as possible, without moving.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	When the bone is dislocated, if it is not reduced within seven days, and it is oiled and greased on all sides, until the dislocation is reduced; then it is reduced, and the manner of reducing it, if you place the splint on the swelling, then assemble the arm on the helper, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and then reduce it with the helper and the arm, if the arm is in its place, nothing will deter you, or if the bone is not movable.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone does not move, if you use splints, and place the fracture on a larger and stronger splint than the others, and have between each splint one of spacers of bone or wood, and each spacer be as large as it passes over the fracture three times; then reduce the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter, more firmly and less by moving them apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	If you see the seating of the elbow, and the stretching, as we have said, in the part that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the aposteme chaut, if you let it alone for one day, if we have said; then look at each third day the link, that prurite does not inflame or come to the elbow because it is too estrois.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.

de la brisure du bras	of the wrist fracture

The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "little" and "big" humerus, of one of which is smaller and forms the pocket; and the other is larger and is the one that is out of place, either the small or the large humerus, by chance.

de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	The following sentence should be translated as: "of the fracture of the bone

de brisure avec plaie	Of a fracture with wound

And if the patient comes, and the burning of vitriol comes, then leave the restoration until the next day, as long as the burning is calmed, and do not touch it again on the third or fourth day, because you will cause the patient to come by accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone is broken, it should be set as soon as possible, so that you can gently place it at your fingertips, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not easy to make with your fingers, then use this instrument made of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and the width should be according to the size of the wound. For this reason, it is necessary to pierce three or four times, according to how many times it is necessary for each treatment of fracture; and it should be sharp and large, so that it does not slip with the compression on the member at your fingertips, and it should also be in front, and large before, and in front:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called "palinthe", because it aims that the heads of the bones be placed on the head of the bone; and the bone once, as long as it rises, and is even, and meets with the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is not clear, and the splints cannot well grasp the bone, then it comes that you cover the head of the bone with the splint, as long as the splints have power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you do not manage to bring the bone back, as we have said, if it is covered with an instrument suitable for this, or cutting and sharp, then use this which is harder in the bone's roughness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, one should suspect that there is something wrong with its natural joint.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you stretch it too much, then drape it in a piece of black, synthetic leather, and do it properly; and do not put anything on the wound or other places where there is oil, so that it does not cause rotting and corruption; then after resetting the bone, leave the wound open, cover it with a cloth, according to the size of the wound, and make sure the wound is not tightened with the fracture; and many times have I seen this happen, and they have brought it to the patient or died or corrupted never; and the scars are softer and less affected than the others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	When the wound is large or severe, and you doubt that it will heal, as we have said, and you feel pain in the leg, but cannot put on a bandage; then wrap the leg with cloth, tie it tightly, and apply poultices.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	When you see after the first or second day that the wound has healed, if all that you have applied has helped, and you have an ointment for healing wounds, such as a medicinal ointment and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to unwrap the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is swollen and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	It is necessary that the limbs be aligned in a certain way that the belly corresponds lightly to the leg.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If they continue to twist, and it cannot be held but rather moves away from the belly, with small pieces of bones, as if it wants to pull the wound with a tent, and all these pieces displaced that cause this pain, then...
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if an abscess comes to the limb, or in some other way of corruption, and you cure it according to what is written in this chapter before, then...
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed through the limb, if it is like the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar bones of the large limbs, if it is not treated because many times death comes but it is left as long as it bleeds; by chance it may heal after 20 or 30 years, and then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of brushes that come out of the heat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come many times after the health of the bracelet, moreover when it is near the joint, and the matter to be seen is the figure of the member; and by chance cannot make the member its natural place.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If you are cold: if you administer strengthening medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolle, and other similar things, either none of these, or all together, and mix them with warm strengthening wine or with plenty of beer or with honey; and then apply them to the wound, and draw it well, and do not let it drip from your hands; and then draw it, and resume another, as long as the swelling is great; or you draw a piece of plaster well made; for the property of the plaster is that it all clots the blood in the members; and if the swelling has turned into hardness, and is becoming like a piercing, and it is bleeding from the wound, then you should cut off any excess; or you leave it on any part that is swollen, as long as it is swollen, and cure it as soon as it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The first sentence to translate is: "ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture is set, and subsides after the weak limbs and soften, if it happens for various reasons: either because one was too tightly bound, and not as it should have been; or because it had too many ligatures, and could not come to the member; or because of excessive inflammation; or because of too many movements at the wrong time; or because there is little blood in the body, and it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is if you make the masseter muscle tense and make the body stiff, as long as it does not multiply in itself; then give a bath, and relax; then put poultice on the limb, if it attracts to the great inflammation, and the swelling often turns green, as the inflammation reaches the member; and realign to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	A dislocated limb after a sudden injury.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is swollen after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is distorted, it does not follow its natural course: if one does not believe the folk who say that the bone must be broken all at once, and many have done this in our land; and these fractures cause great harm, and by chance the patient dies; however, if the wounds and torments are fresh, and it is necessary to raise them with hot water, or herbs that soften, as with nettles, and roots, and honey, and similar things; and I apply a softening ointment, as well made as dyaquilon, and take the vismalve muscillaige and cook it with lard or oil of sisament, and apply it thus; or take fat figs and chew them with colon fiber, and similar medicines that dry the urine.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never has been seen a node that is constantly and continuously tightened with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be no movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is awakened and hardened, like a wound, and there is need of the forge, then it comes to pass that the coper meets with the bone, in the subtle incision lightly; and it is necessary to strengthen and study in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs at no joint, it comes to bring sense to the member.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, and by chance it is caught in the joint, and when it is reset, it is often moved to the shoulder; therefore, if it cannot be moved back to its place when it is enlarged: many times come pain and other sufferings; then, as soon as this happens, I make the patient better, then leave it, until the abscess is closed and healed; then warm the member with oil, then reset it gently, and cure each member as well as it was cured in its joint.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the surgeons to treat the dislocations of the shoulder joints.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	There are two ways in which the mandibles are dislocated: either they are slightly broken at their bases and become soft; or they are completely dislocated and hang downwards, and the saliva from the mouth cannot be held, and the mouth cannot be closed, and the tongue is wrapped around with the speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	If the dislocation is small, it returns through more positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	If the dislocation is complete and fixed, then it must be reset as soon as possible without force; in such a way that the patient's shoulder joint is marked with the other hand at the root of the mandible dislocating the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands are deformed to make them equal; and command the patient to make the mandibles soft and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the measure is equal, as it is in its place in his shoulder.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is reset gritty, then it is the same as the two mandibles together, if the arrows of hot and oily oil are applied, until they are lightly reset; do not worry about how rough the reset is, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset correctly, and the patient's mouth feels very soft, if you apply warm and oily drapes made of oil and wax to the mouth, then gently close it with threads; and let the patient lie on his back, and his head between the two pillows, so that he does not move to the right or left, and does not force himself to breathe, but eats light meat as long as the pain is steady and does not affect the jaws; and then do what you have gently reset, and do not try to open the mouth with your teeth and tongue, as long as the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be repositioned at once in an hour, and are not converted to their proper positions, then if fevers and customary colds come, and by chance the stomach, and by chance vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then you will know that it is a mistake; and many times died those who came, in nine years.
de la forcelle	of the force.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The force cannot be removed from the cost of the continuation of the hand and the foot, and it is never stable at the end, and that is felt by everyone.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is if the patient is able to hold his back straight and extend his arms; then press the shoulder to your palm, and it will return; then place the splint and bandage on it, and tighten; and the joint that is towards the elbow cannot be dislocated; if not, and if it is never dislocated, then reset it to the shoulder, as we have said; then place the splint and bandage on it, and tighten, and command the patient to rest as soon as he is healthy; and then you will realign the head of the shoulder when it is able to be removed from its socket.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	The first sentence to translate is "de la dislocation de l’espaule". The translation is 
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	The translation of "Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres" is: "Ways to dislocate the shoulder are known in three ways: either it is dislocated at the part of the axlebox at the desoz; or it is dislocated at the part of the pis; or it is dislocated at the part of the sus, and this happens rarely; or it does not dislocate the shoulder from the shoulder, nor does it dislocate the tendons; and more often it dislocates towards the axlebox, nevertheless to those who have little strength, because in this jump it is most helpful; to those who have enough strength, it jumps at points, and returns to points.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, it happens to some men that they are struck or castrated, and the arm swells from an abscess, and make sure it is not dislocated due to this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you examine it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And know the dislocations when they are towards the axis, and make a difference between the sick arm and the healthy one, and you will find between them clear differences; and you will find at the top of the arm a hollow, and down the axis to the top of the arm, as if it were some ones; and he cannot bring his hand back to its place, nor move without any movements; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, if it is not hidden, because you can see it clearly at the top; and this way of dislocation is not far to bring back, when it is new, or if it is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The manner is that the nurse gently places her hand on the shoulder of the patient, then removes your hands from the wound, and gently releases the joint at the top of the shoulder; the nurse then gently places her hand there, extends it upwards, and places it above, if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in our hands shortly after, then it is that the patient should be bathed in warm water; the wound will be softened and soothed, as with a decoction of aloe and fenugreek and honey in warm water, and it will become soft; then the patient is wrapped on his back, and a piece of linen is placed on the wound, not too soft nor too hard, then the foot of the patient is placed on the linen, and the shoulder is gently lifted by the hand of the nurse, and the muscles of the shoulder are eased; other nurses may trace the shoulder with their finger to see if it does not move; this shoulder now returns, and if you see that it is presented in this way: and that you make present to the patient a larger shield than the nurse's hand; then the shield should be placed on the shoulder of the patient, and the shoulder should be lifted up, so that the nurse's hand hangs down towards the belly; other nurses may trace the shoulder with their hand towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too weak, if there is nothing heavy that can be done with them, then the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the reduction can also be done in another way: and it is like finding a long tusk in the ground, whose head is also returned as if it were a pistol; then it is placed on the patient's shoulder, but if it is not too large or too heavy; then the shoulder is extended from the other side, forming the joint again; and if it does not return to its place for all these things that we have said, then this treatment must be done: take a tusk of two fingers in length and four in width, which has its root enter into the palm of the hand from behind the shoulder, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie the head of the wrist that was not bent by the maid, then place it in the palm of the maid; and extend some arms over the long wrist, and the helper over the shoulder of the arm, then put the arm over the elbow of an arrow, and extend the hands on the other side, and let the chest hang down from another part: the joint was now straightened.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi. And when the dislocation is in front, if it is necessary to extend the painful leg strongly, as I have said; and then place the patient's hand on the painful knee, and pull back towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the back, if it cannot be extended the leg backward, do not get up from the ground, as we have said for the hips; and place your hand on your face, and extend the limb as we have said before, and must press on the joint at the table; and when the leg is extended, it will be equal; then bend the knees, and insert the splint, and hold with a bandage, if the knee does not move; and rest for three or four hours, then remove the splint, and see if the legs are equal, if the stretch, as we have said before, and let it remain for three or four hours; then remove the bandage, and send the patient home when the limbs are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the shoulder dislocation of the first kind
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: it should be pulled downwards and backwards, and not from the front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if you command the patient to bend their leg at the knee, and it does not bend at the knee, then it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient right, and extend the leg if possible, and put your back on your heel, and put your foot on your thighs; then take the shoulder with your hands, and stretch between your two fingers, and bend the two thumbs that form the first part of the shoulder; and other means extend the foot, as long as the shoulder returns to its place, and the signs are that the knee is slightly bent; and apply the plaster, and make the leg bend at the knee, and assemble the fingers firmly three or four times, then release it; and do not move the patient's limbs too much until they are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not present, if there is extension of the limb, as we have said in the treatment of the gout, as soon as it is healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the big toe
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The big toe is never used, and it is never completely dislocated, and it is often damaged and deformed.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is that if the ankle is swollen, and it should be examined before the part where it is dislocated: the remedies are light, and they should be extended gently with the hands as soon as it is only available.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, if you should place the ankle straight in the right position, and hold it with your hand by the knee, and then pull the foot to you with your left hand, and then with your right hand, and raise it twice, and then place it back on your thumb; and do this twice, as we have said, with a gentle touch and raising the foot; if it returns, it is well; if not, if it does not return, you must repeat the dislocation, for it will return; and if it cannot return, you should place the ankle on its back against the ground, and hold the knee firmly on the ground between the knees, and draw the leg outwards so that the ankle does not bleed; then mark the ministers with your thumb, and extend the foot to your hands or to the other hand, where it is at the top of the ankle; then extend all the ministers equally, and the passenger should be held between the knees of the ankle; then extend each minister equally, and the passenger should be held between the knees of the ankle to hold the ankle in place; then place the dislocation in your hands, and mark the healthy leg at the other end, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	When it reaches the point, if it is plastered and allowed to dry, and forms, and the bandage is tied around the leg, and warded the nerves that are under the ankle bone, so as not to be too tight; then it is left on for two or three days, and if it remains tight, then it is loosened; then it is removed at the end of the fourth or fifth day, and the patient is given instructions to change the bandage every four days. If it is still tight, it is loosened again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If abscesses form, and if they come, then it is necessary to relax them, as we have said before, as long as they are healthy.
des dois	Of two things, one is that the
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	If the two are dislocated, if they are managed well, and it is a light thing to extend the sense of work.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocations are in no pain or strain, then it is best to make the patient lie on his back or on his side, and place your foot on what opens these joints, then press with your foot until it returns; and when it is equalized, and there is no opening, then place the sole of your foot on the patient's shoulder blade, and form the foot, and let it stay for three hours, then remove it; and then rest, as long as it is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, often the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in your treatment, if you are not ignorant or cruel and slow, and if you are compassionate and merciful and tardy, do not be proud; and begin with calming measures for the wound, and let the patient hold the hand of God; when you see hope for health, reset the limb to the shoulder, unless the wound bleeds and moves; when the limb is at the shoulder, if the wound is calmed and treated, and the pain is lessened, as it should be in simple diseases, and if there is a fracture with the dislocation, and the bones are broken, do what we have said in simple diseases; and do not enter into a state of despair, according to what we have said, for this is according to your creator's will, and for the wisdom of your heart.
